Praying on a Mat with Images: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Dislikedness
Ruling on praying on a mat with pictures, with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two Hanafi positions on praying on a mat with images and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
The ruling depends on whether images are of living beings and whether they are treated with contempt.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between the authors of Al-Asl and Al-Mabsut regarding the dislikedness (karahah) of praying on a mat containing pictures. The key issue is whether the presence of images inherently detracts from the sanctity of prayer, or whether it can be mitigated by showing contempt for the images. We will examine both positions and the reconciliation based on the type of image.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting Hanafi views
Note that Al-Asl states it is not disliked, provided one shows contempt for the pictures and does not prostrate on them. Al-Mabsut states it is absolutely disliked, regardless of prostration.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf within the same school.
2
Understand the basis of each view
Al-Asl's view is based on commanding humiliation of images, while Al-Mabsut emphasizes the honor of the prayer mat and the inappropriateness of images in worship.
Both use proofs from the command to degrade images, but differ on applicability.
3
Recognize the practical difference: prostration on the image
Al-Asl allows prayer if one avoids prostrating on the image; Al-Mabsut forbids it even if prostration is avoided. The dispute centers on whether the mere presence of images is problematic.
4
Apply the distinction between living and non-living beings
The passage reconciles by limiting the dislikedness to images of living beings (dhawi al-ruh). Images of non-living things are not disliked, citing Ibn Abbas.
This distinction is crucial for practical application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تصویر والے بچھونے پر نماز پڑھنا مکروہ نہیں
دار اطلق الكراهية في الاصل لان المصلى معظم اليونان يصلى على بساط فيه تصاوير، لان فيه استهانة بالصور ولا يسجد على التصاوير لانه يشبه عبادة
اور اسے چھونے پر نماز پڑھنے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں جس میں تصویریں بنی ہوں کیونکہ ایسا کرنے میں تصویروں کی تحقیر اور توہین کرنا ہے اور سجدہ تصویر پر نہ کرے کیونکہ یہ تصویر کی پرستش کے مشابہ ہے۔ اور مبسوط میں کراہت کو مطلق لکھا ہے کیونکہ جائے نماز کیا کچھ ہے جس پر تصویریں بنی ہوں اس پر نماز پڑھنے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں یعنی بلا کراہت جائز ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ ایسا کرنے میں تصویروں کی تحقیر اور تذلیل کرنا ہے اور ہم کو اس بات کا حکم کیا گیا ہے کہ اگر کوئی نادان جاندار کی تصویر بنا کر حماقت نامے کے تصویر کو ذلیل و خوار سمجھیں اور اس کے ساتھ ذلت اور توہین کا برتاؤ کریں۔
مصنف کہتے ہیں کہ سجدہ تصویر پر نہ کرے کیونکہ یہ تصویر کی پرستش کے مشابہ ہے۔ جامع صغیر کی اس عبارت کا حاصل یہ نہیں کہ بچھونے پر نماز تو پڑھے لیکن سجدہ تصویر پر نہ کرے۔ مبسوط میں لکھا ہے کہ تصویر دار بچھونے پر نماز پڑھنا مطلقا مکروہ ہے خواہ تصویر پر سجدہ کرے یا نہ کرے، اور دلیل یہ ذکر کی کہ نماز کے لئے تیار کیا گیا ہے یعنی مصلی فی نفسہ معظم اور مکرم ہے۔ پس اگر اس میں تصویریں ہوں گی تو ان تصویروں کی ایک آئے گی حالانکہ ہم کو ان کی اہانت کا حکم کیا گیا ہے۔ اس لئے جائے نماز پر تصویروں کا ہونا مطلقا مناسب نہیں خواہ اس تصویر پر سجدہ نہ کرے۔
فائدہ: تصویر وہ ہوتی ہے جو مخلوق خدا کے مشابہ بنائی گئی ہو خواہ ذی روح کی ہو یا غیر ذی روح کی۔ اور تمثال ذی روح کے ساتھ خاص ہے لیکن یہاں ذی روح کی تصویر مراد ہے کیونکہ غیر ذی روح کی تصویر میں کوئی کراہت نہیں ہے کیونکہ ابن عباس نے ایک مصور سے کہا تھا: {إِنْ كُنْتَ لَا بُدَّ فَاعِلًا فَعَلَيْكَ بِتَمْثَالِ غَيْرِ ذِي الرُّوحِ} یعنی اگر تجھ کو تصویر بنانا ہی ہے تو غیر ذی روح کی تصویر بنا لیا کر۔ (فتح القدیر)
Praying on a mat with pictures is not disliked. Dar declared dislikedness in Al-Asl because the worshiper is honored, he prays on a mat containing pictures because it shows contempt for the pictures, and he should not prostrate on the pictures because it resembles worship. There is no harm in praying on a mat on which pictures are made because in doing so there is degradation and humiliation of the pictures. And he should not prostrate on the picture because it resembles worship of the picture. And in Al-Mabsut, dislikedness is stated absolutely because the prayer mat is something; praying on a mat with pictures on it is not harmful, meaning it is permissible without dislike. The proof is that in doing so there is degradation and humiliation of the pictures, and we have been commanded that if someone ignorant makes a picture of a living being and regards the picture as lowly and contemptible and treats it with degradation and humiliation.
The author says that one should not prostrate on the picture because it resembles worship of the picture. The gist of the passage from Al-Jami' al-Saghir is not that he prays on the mat but does not prostrate on the picture. In Al-Mabsut it is written that praying on a mat with pictures is absolutely disliked, whether he prostrates on the picture or not, and the proof given is that it is prepared for prayer, i.e., the worshiper in himself is honored and respected. So if there are pictures on it, then those pictures will be something, although we have been commanded to humiliate them. Therefore, the presence of pictures on the prayer mat is absolutely not appropriate, even if he does not prostrate on the picture.
Benefit: A picture (taswir) is that which is made resembling God's creation, whether of a living being or not. And timthal is specific to living beings. But here, the picture of a living being is meant because there is no dislike in a picture of a non-living being. Because Ibn Abbas said to a painter: {If you must do, then make images of non-living things} meaning if you must make images, then make images of non-living things. (Fath al-Qadir)
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof about praying on a mat that contains pictures. The author initially states that it is not disliked (makruh) to pray on such a mat, provided that one shows contempt for the pictures (by stepping on them or sitting on them) and does not prostrate directly on the picture, as that would resemble worship. The proof is that we are commanded to degrade images of living beings, not to honor them. However, the author then reports a difference: Al-Mabsut (by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani) states that it is absolutely disliked, regardless of whether one prostrates on the picture, because the mat is meant for prayer, which is an act of worship, and having pictures on it goes against the solemnity of prayer. The author reconciles by noting that the dislike applies only to pictures of living beings (dhawi al-ruh), as per the hadith of Ibn Abbas. Pictures of non-living things (trees, mountains, etc.) are not disliked. The Hanafi mufta bihi is more nuanced: it is permissible but better to avoid, and one should avoid prostrating on pictures of living beings.

Key Terms
تصویر (taṣwīr): An image or picture, specifically of a living being (dhawi al-ruh) in this context.
تمثال (timthāl): An image or statue of a living being.
ذی روح (dhī rūḥ): A living being, literally 'possessor of soul'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is absolutely disliked (makruh tanzihi).
B) It is permissible without any dislike.
C) It is invalid (batil).
D) It is obligatory to avoid.

Key Takeaway
Praying on a mat with images of living beings is makruh tanzihi; images of non-living things are not disliked, according to the reconciled Hanafi position.

Images in the Prayer Area: A Ruling on Dislikedness
Ruling with proof on images in the prayer area

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying with visible images of living beings, identify the exception for small images, and apply the proof from the hadith of Jibra'il.

Core Idea
Prayer with visible images of living beings is valid but disliked, except when the image is too small to be worshipped.

When we pray, we seek the presence of divine mercy and angels. The presence of images of living beings is considered an obstacle for angels, based on the well-known hadith of Jibra'il. In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position that such prayer is valid (sahih) but disliked (makruh tanzihi), and we explore the proof and the exception for very small images.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is praying while images of living beings are visible in front, above, or to the sides of the worshiper. The ruling is makruh tanzihi (light dislikedness) – the prayer is valid but discouraged.
The dislikedness applies only to images of living beings (dhawat al-arwah).
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith of Jibra'il (Gabriel) from Abu Hurairah, in which Jibra'il refuses to enter the Prophet's house due to a curtain with pictures. This hadith is the primary proof.
The hadith text is provided in the passage: 'استاذن جبرئيل النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم...'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith shows that angels avoid houses containing images of living beings. Since prayer is an act seeking angelic presence and blessings, the presence of such images makes the prayer disliked, but not invalid.
The inference is not that the prayer is rejected, but that the environment is less conducive to reverence.
4
Note the exception for small images
If the image is so small that it is not apparent to the observer, it is not disliked, because such small images are not objects of veneration.
The text says: 'ولو كانت الصورة صغيرة بحيث لا تبدو للناظر لا يكره'.
5
Apply the ruling to practical scenarios
Evaluate real-life cases: a large painting on the wall, a small sticker, a defaced image (head cut off). Determine the ruling based on visibility and size.
The hadith also suggests solutions: cut off the head or use the image as a mat to show contempt.

و يكره ان يكون فوق رأسه فى السقف او بین یدیه او بحذائه تصاویر او صورة معلقة لحديث جرب ندخل بيتا فيه كلب او صورة ولو كانت الصورة صغيرة بحيث لا تبدو للناظر لا يكره لان الصغار جدا . ترجمہ: اور مکروہ ہے یہ کہ مصلی کے سر کے اوپر چھت میں یا اس کے سامنے یا اس کے دائیں بائیں تصویریں ہوں یا کوئی تصویر لٹکی ہو۔ کیونکہ حدیث جبرئیل ہے کہ ہم ایسے گھر میں داخل نہیں ہوتے جس میں کتا ہو یا تصویر ہو۔ اور اگر تصویر اس قدر چھوٹی ہے جو دیکھنے والے کو ظاہر نہ ہو تو مکروہ نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ بہت ہی چھوٹی تصویر میں پوجی نہیں جاتیں۔
تشریح: فرمایا کہ مصلی کے سر کے اوپر چھت میں یا سامنے یا اس کے دائیں بائیں اگر تصویریں ہوں تو اس میں نماز پڑھنا تصویری کی ہو تو بھی نماز مکروہ ہے۔ دلیل حدیث جبرئیل ہے عن ابي هريرة رضى الله تعالى عنه انه قال استاذن جبرو النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال ادخل فقال كيف ادخل وفی بیتک سترفيه تصاوير ما ان تقلع رأسها صــ بساطاً يوطا فانا معاشره الملائكة لاندخل بيتا فيه تصاوير . (شرح نقایه) یعنی حضرت ابو ہریرہ نے فرمایا کہ جبرئیل نے اللہ کے نبی سے اجازت مانگی، حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا کہ داخل ہو جاؤ، جبرئیل نے کہا کس طرح داخل ہوں حالانکہ آپ کے گھر میں ایک پردہ ہے جس میں تصویریں ہیں، یا تو ان کا سر کاٹ دیا جائے یا بچھونے بنا دیئے جائیں جو جابجا بچھائے جائیں۔ کیونکہ ہم جماعت ملائکہ ایسے گھر میں داخل نہیں ہوتے جس میں تصویریں ہوں۔ اس حدیث سے اس طور پر استدلال ہوگا کہ جس مکان میں ملائکہ داخل نہیں ہوتے وہ مکان شر البیوت ہوتا ہے اور نماز
And it is disliked if above his head in the ceiling, or in front of him, or beside him there are pictures or a hanging picture, because of the hadith of Jibra'il: 'We do not enter a house in which there is a dog or a picture.' And if the picture is so small that it is not apparent to the viewer, then it is not disliked because very small pictures are not worshipped. Explanation: He said that if there are pictures above the worshiper's head in the ceiling, or in front, or to his right or left, then praying with such pictures is disliked. The proof is the hadith of Jibra'il from Abu Hurairah (may Allah be pleased with him) that Jibra'il asked permission from the Prophet (peace be upon him), and he said 'Enter'. Jibra'il said 'How can I enter when in your house there is a curtain with pictures? Either cut off their heads or make them into mats that are stepped on, because we, the company of angels, do not enter a house in which there are pictures.' (Sharh al-Niqayah) The inference from this hadith is that a house in which angels do not enter is an evil house, and prayer... (incomplete)
Source pages p. 159

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof about the dislikedness of having images (pictures of living beings) in the area where one prays. The author states that it is makruh (disliked) to have pictures above the head (on the ceiling), in front, or to the sides of the worshiper. The proof is a hadith in which Jibra'il (Gabriel) refuses to enter a house containing a picture of a living being. However, the text adds an exception: if the picture is very small so that it does not appear to the observer, then it is not disliked because it is too small to be worshipped. The comment from Sharh al-Niqayah provides the full hadith text, which offers two solutions: either cut off the head of the picture (making it inanimate) or turn it into a mat that is stepped on (to show contempt). The Hanafi ruling is that such pictures should be avoided in the prayer area to ensure the presence of angels and blessings. If they are present and visible, the prayer is valid but disliked. This applies regardless of whether the image is hung or on a wall; only small, inconspicuous images are exempt.

Key Terms
مکروہ (makrūh): Disliked; an act that is discouraged but not sinful. The prayer is valid but less rewardable.
تصویر (taṣwīr): An image of a living being (the context specifies ذی روح).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a person prays in front of a very small picture (less than a fingertip) of a bird hanging on the wall?
A) The prayer is invalid because the picture is of a living being.
B) The prayer is valid and not disliked because the picture is too small to be worshipped.
C) The prayer is valid but disliked because any picture is problematic.
D) The prayer is only disliked if the picture is behind the worshiper.

Key Takeaway
Prayer in the presence of visible images of living beings is valid but disliked (makruh tanzihi); very small or inconspicuous images are exempt.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Images in Prayer: General Ruling and Exception for Tiny Images
Explains the ruling on images in prayer area and the exception for tiny images

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on images in prayer and identify when a tiny image is exempt from dislike.

Core Idea
Images in prayer area are makruh; tiny images that do not appear are not.

This lesson examines two related rulings from Ashraf al-Hidayah: first, images of animate beings in the prayer area are makruh tanzih; second, very small images that are not noticeable are exempt. The evidence includes the hadith of Jibril and the story of Daniyal's ring.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling: praying with images in the area
The act is praying while images (taswir of animate beings) are present above the head, in front, or to the side of the worshiper. The ruling is makruh tanzih (disliked, not sinful).
Makruh tanzih means the prayer is valid (sahih) but it is better to avoid it.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The hadith of Jibril (from Abu Huraira): 'We angels do not enter a house with images.' This indicates that such a house is disliked, and thus prayer there is disliked.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) and its interpretation is zanni.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith implies that images attract the absence of angels of mercy, making the place less blessed. Hanafi scholars extend this to the prayer area, concluding that prayer is makruh.
Some scholars limit this to large or prominent images.
4
Identify the exception for very small images
If the image is very small (صغيرة جداً) such that it does not appear to the viewer (لا تبدو للناظر), then it is not disliked. The rationale is that such images do not invite veneration.
Supporting evidence: the ring of Daniyal (peace be upon him) had tiny images and was kept by Umar (may Allah be pleased with him).
5
Apply the rulings
In practice, one should avoid large, prominent images in the prayer area. Tiny images on rings or carpets that are not noticeable are permissible.
The mufta bihi position is that the prayer is valid but disliked for large images; small images are completely free of dislike.

بنوایا تا کہ اس کو دیکھ کر ہمہ وقت اللہ کی نعمتیں یاد رہیں۔ حضرت ابو موسیٰ اشعری کے حوالہ سے یہ واقعہ بھی ظاہر ہوا کہ بہت چھوٹی تصویر کا گھر میں رکھنا مکروہ نہیں ہے ورنہ حضرت عمر رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ حضرت دانیال کی یہ انگوٹھی کیونکر رکھوانے دیتے۔
Chapter on what invalidates prayer and what is disliked in it. Ashraf al-Hidayah: The meaning of images is humiliating them, and we are commanded to treat them with disrespect. The author says: Do not prostrate on an image because it resembles worship. From al-Jami al-Saghir: One may pray on a mat but not prostrate on an image. In al-Mabsut: Praying on a mat with images is absolutely disliked, whether one prostrates on the image or not. The reasoning: The prayer mat is prepared for prayer, and the praying person is honored, but images on it would be honored while we are commanded to disrespect them. Image is what resembles God's creatures, whether animate or inanimate. But 'tamthal' is specific to animate beings; here animate image is meant, as inanimate images are not disliked. Ibn Abbas told a painter: 'If you must, make images of inanimate things.' (Fath al-Qadir) It is disliked to have images above the head in the ceiling, in front, or to the side, due to the hadith of Jibril: 'We do not enter a house with a dog or an image.' If the image is very small so that it does not appear to the viewer, it is not disliked. Explanation: The hadith is from Abu Huraira: Jibril sought permission, and the Prophet said enter, but Jibril said 'How can I enter when you have a curtain with images? Either cut off their heads or make them into mats for treading.' We angels do not enter a house with images. This proves such a house is evil, and prayer there is disliked. Angels of mercy do not separate from humans except at relieving oneself and intercourse. Support: Abu Huraira had a ring with two lions. The story of Daniyal's ring: During Umar's caliphate, Daniyal's (peace be upon him) ring was found. It had a lion, lioness, and a child, showing them licking the child. Umar wept and gave it to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari. This story shows that a very small image is not disliked, otherwise Umar would not have kept that ring.
Source pages p. 159

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah is an expansion on the ruling about images in the prayer area. The author begins by stating the fundamental principle: images must be disrespected, and we are commanded to humiliate them. Therefore, prostrating on an image is disliked because it implies veneration. The matn from al-Mabsut clarifies that praying on a mat with images is absolutely disliked (makruh), whether one prostrates on the image or not, because the mat is an honored object for prayer and images on it would be dishonored. The exception for non-animate images is based on the hadith of Ibn Abbas. The second ruling addresses images in the ceiling, in front, or to the side of the worshiper. The hadith of Jibril is cited, stating that angels do not enter a house with images. The Hanafi scholars interpret this dislike as makruh tanzih. However, if the image is very small and not apparent, it is not disliked, as it does not invite veneration. The story of Daniyal's ring, narrated by Fath al-Qadir and others, supports this: Umar allowed the ring with an image of a lion and lioness because the image was tiny and not meant for worship. This shows that the Hanafi position balances textual evidence with practical reasoning.

Key Terms
تصویر (taswir): An image or picture that resembles a created being, whether animate or inanimate.
مکروہ (makruh): Disliked; an act that is not sinful but should be avoided. In this context, makruh tanzih.
تمثال (timthal): A statue or image, specifically of a living being with a soul.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this lesson, which of the following images in the prayer area is NOT disliked (makruh)?
A) A large painting of a horse in front of the worshiper.
B) A small image on a ring that is not noticeable.
C) A statue of a lion above the worshiper's head.
D) A photograph of a bird on the wall to the right.

Key Takeaway
Images of animate beings in the prayer area are makruh tanzih, but very small, unnoticeable images are exempt; the prayer remains valid in all cases.

Ruling on Headless Images: Permissibility in the Hanafi School
Concludes ruling on headless images with rational proof and lamp analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on headless images and explain the underlying 'illa (effective cause) that permits them.

Core Idea
A headless image loses its status as an object of worship, so the prohibition of karaahah does not apply.

In this passage, the author of al-Hidayah concludes the discussion on images by addressing headless images. The key point is that the ruling of karaahah (dislike) is linked to the potential for veneration. Once the head is removed, the image ceases to be an object of worship, and the prohibition falls away. This lesson will unpack the reasoning and the analogy to praying facing a lamp.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The act is having or praying in the presence of a headless image. The ruling is that there is no karaahah (dislike); it is permissible.
The ruling is mubah (permissible).
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is rational (dalil aqli): a headless image is not worshipped because it lacks a head. Therefore it does not fall under the prohibition of images that are worshipped.
The text explicitly states: 'it is not worshipped without the head.'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does this fact prove permissibility? The 'illa (effective cause) for karaahah is resemblance to objects of worship. A headless image lacks that resemblance.
The analogy to a lamp (which is not worshipped) reinforces the point.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (disagreement)
Some later shuyukh (scholars) reportedly disliked praying facing a lamp, but the author of al-Hidayah does not adopt that view. The headless image ruling is clear.
This shows that ikhtilaf exists on the lamp analogy, but the main ruling is settled.
5
Evaluate the mufta bihi (operative position)
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that headless images are not disliked. This is based on zahir al-riwayah and is the view of Imam al-Marghinani.
Later fatwa works follow this view.

And if the image is headless, i.e., the head is erased, then it is not a statue because it is not worshipped without the head. Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage concludes the discussion on images by addressing headless images. The author states that if an image has its head removed or erased, it ceases to be a 'timthal' (statue) for legal purposes because worship of such an image is not possible. Therefore, the ruling of karaahah (dislike) does not apply. This is analogous to praying facing a lamp or candle, which some shuyukh considered disliked, but the headless image is not disliked because it is not venerated. The main point is that the prohibition or dislike in the Hanafi school is linked to the potential for veneration. Without a head, the image loses its status as an object of worship. This is a practical ruling based on 'illa (effective cause): the reason for karaahah is the resemblance to worship, and a headless image does not incite worship.

Key Terms
مقطوعة الرأس (maqtu'at al-ra's): An image or statue with the head cut off or erased, making it incomplete and not worthy of worship.
شمع یا سراج (sham' aw siraj): Candle or lamp; praying facing a lit candle is compared to headless images, with some shuyukh disliking it, but the opinion of no karaahah for headless images prevails.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is a headless image not disliked in prayer?
A) Because it is not made by a human.
B) Because it cannot be worshipped without a head.
C) Because it is smaller than a handspan.
D) Because it is not on a prayer mat.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits headless images because the reason for prohibition (potential veneration) is absent.

Ruling on Praying in a House with Very Small Images
Expanding the base ruling on images in the prayer space

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying in a house with an image, identify the condition that triggers karahah, and explain the exception for very small images that are not perceptible or venerated.

Core Idea
A very small image that is not visible or respected does not make prayer makruh in the Hanafi school.

This passage from a commentary on al-Hidayah clarifies a common concern: Does having an image in the house invalidate or make prayer disliked? The author explains the general rule based on the hadith about angels of mercy, then carves out an exception for images so small they are not really noticed. The story of Prophet Daniel's ring serves as practical evidence that even the Companions kept such images without karahah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling and its evidence
Locate the statement that praying in a house with an image is makruh and note the hadith proof about angels of mercy not entering. Understand that the karahah is due to loss of blessing, not invalidity.
The hadith is from ahad (single-narrator) sources, so the ruling is zanni in evidence.
2
Analyze the legal cause (illah)
The karahah arises because images prevent angels of mercy from entering. The exception is derived from the absence of this cause: if the image is too small to be a focus of respect or attention, it does not deter the angels.
Hanafi legal reasoning uses istihsan to limit the general rule when the effective cause is missing.
3
Understand the exception for very small images
The text says if an image is so small that it is not apparent to the beholder, there is no karahah. This is because the eye does not fall upon it and it is not treated with reverence.
Size is relative; the key is whether the image is perceived and respected.
4
Examine the corroborating evidence (Daniel's ring)
The story of Caliph Umar approving of Prophet Daniel's ring with a tiny image of lions and a child shows that such images are not makruh. The Companions would not have kept it if it violated the ruling.
This historical precedent strengthens the exception and shows its application in early Islam.
5
Apply the ruling to a modern scenario
Consider a small logo on a prayer mat or a tiny design on a wall. According to this lesson, if the image is not conspicuous or venerated, the prayer is not makruh.
One must judge based on common custom: what is considered a significant image.

Source Text

Chapter: What Invalidates Prayer and What is Disliked in It. So it is makruh, therefore praying in such a house is makruh. Keep in mind that in the hadith, by 'angels' is meant the angels of mercy, and they are never separated from a human except at two times: one at the time of relieving oneself, and the second at the time of being with one's wife. (Sharh Niqayah) If an image is so small that it is not apparent to the beholder, there is no karahah, because the eye does not fall upon a very small image. So [it is as] if the image on the bedspread is not in sight. And this is also supported by the fact that Hadrat Abu Huraira (may Allah be pleased with him) had a ring on which was engraved the image of two children. The incident of the ring of Prophet Daniel: An incident mentioned by the author of Fath al-Qadir, the author of Kifayah, and Mulla Ali Qari is that during the caliphate of Umar al-Azam (may Allah be pleased with him), the ring of Prophet Daniel (peace be upon him) (who had passed away) was found. On that ring were two lions, and between them a child. The image showed that the lion and lioness both were licking the child. When Umar al-Azam saw this, his eyes welled up with tears, and he gave that ring to Hadrat Abu Musa al-Ash'ari (may Allah be pleased with him). The background of this incident is that when Bakht Nasr ascended the throne, a soothsayer informed him that a child would be born who would kill him. So Bakht Nasr began to kill every newborn child. When the mother of Daniel gave birth to Daniel, fearing for his life, she left him in a barren wilderness. In that desolate wilderness, there was no human being except the True Nurturer. Allah, the Great and Exalted, arranged for the education and protection of that innocent child and future source of guidance and direction by sending a lion to guard him from wild animals and a lioness to nurse him. Both of them would lick that noble child. Later, Daniel (peace be upon him) had this image engraved on his ring so that whenever he saw it, he would remember Allah's blessings. From this incident it also became clear that keeping a very small image in the house is not makruh; otherwise, Hadrat Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) would not have [kept] Daniel's ring.
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage combines a ruling statement from the matn (prayer in a house with a dog or image is makruh because angels of mercy do not enter) with an expansion from the sharh clarifying two exceptions: (1) angels only leave at two specific private moments, so the hadith does not imply complete absence; (2) if the image is so small it is not visible or not considered a real image, there is no karahah. The story of Daniel's ring serves as historical evidence that a tiny image (a lion and child on a ring) was kept by the Prophet's Companion Abu Musa al-Ash'ari with the approval of Caliph Umar, indicating it is not makruh. The lesson establishes that the karahah relates to disrespect or association with idolatry; a minuscule image that is not venerated does not trigger the prohibition.

Key Terms
كراهة (karahah): In this context, makruh means disliked (tanzih) – the prayer is valid but it is better to avoid it due to the absence of blessings.
ملائكة رحمت (mala'ikat al-rahmat): The angels of mercy who bring blessings and forgiveness. They do not enter houses with dogs or images.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as explained in this lesson, what is the ruling on praying in a house where there is a very small image that is not apparent to the beholder?
A) The prayer is invalid (batil).
B) The prayer is valid but makruh tanzih.
C) The prayer is valid and not makruh because the image is not considered significant.
D) The prayer is mustahabb.

Key Takeaway
Praying with a very small, imperceptible image in the house is neither invalid nor disliked in the Hanafi school; the karahah applies only to images that are visible and treated with respect.

Rulings on Decapitated Images and Praying Facing a Lamp
States the ruling on two makruh scenarios in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on decapitated images and explain the preferred view on praying facing a lamp, applying the ta'lil (effective cause) of karahah.

Core Idea
Karahah hinges on veneration; no karahah without worship.

This passage from al-Hidayah discusses two scenarios that might be considered makruh during prayer: the presence of a decapitated image and facing a lamp or candle. The Hanafi school resolves both by examining the underlying cause (ta'lil): karahah only applies when the object is an object of veneration. Since a headless image lacks the focus of worship and a lamp is not worshipped, the preferred view is that there is no karahah. This lesson walks through the reasoning and notes the intra-Hanafi difference on the lamp issue.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings and their common principle
Both rulings are tied to the concept of 'ibadah (worship/veneration). The absence of karahah in both cases stems from the object not being an object of worship.
2
Analyze the ruling on decapitated images
The head is the locus of respect; an image without a head is not venerated. Hence, it is legally not an image (timthal) but an inanimate object, so no karahah.
This follows from the principle that karahah in prayer due to images is because they distract or resemble idols, but a headless figure does not.
3
Examine the ikhtilaf on praying facing a lamp
Some earlier Hanafi mashayikh considered it makruh by analogy to fire-worship. However, the preferred view (raajih) rejects this because a lamp is not an object of worship; the effective cause (idolatry) is absent.
The analogy to fire fails because fire is worshipped, lamps are not.
4
Evaluate the tarjih (preferred view)
The later authorities (mutakhkhirin) settled on no karahah, and this is the mufta bihi (operative ruling) for fatwa.
This is based on the ta'lil of 'ibadah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سرکئی یا سرمٹی تصویر کے حکم میں نہیں
سالی شمع او سراج على ما قالوا كان التمثال مقطوع الرأس اى ممحو الرأس فليس بتمثال لانه لا تعبد بدون الرأس و صاركما اذا

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو دایه
کے آگے رکھنے میں کراہت کی وجہ یہی تھی کہ اس کی پرستش کی جاتی ہو۔ پس جب یہ وجہ نہیں پائی گئی تو کراہت بھی نہیں ہوئی۔
نے یہی کہا ہے۔ بعض حضرات کا قول یہ ہے کہ سامنے موم بتی یا چراغ رکھ کر نماز پڑھنا مکروہ ہے جیسا کہ اگر مصلی کے سامنے انگیٹھی ہواور کی دیکتے ہوئے انگارے ہوں یا شعلہ زن آگ ہوتو یہ مکروہ ہے لیکن بیح قول عدم کراہت کا ہے۔
It is not in the ruling of a headless image. Some [scholars] said that if an image is decapitated, i.e., the head is erased, it is not an image because it is not worshipped without a head, and it becomes as if... If one prays facing a candle or lamp based on what some mashayikh said. When an image has its head cut off, i.e., the head is obliterated, it is not an image, because an image is not referred to without the head. And this becomes like... If an image has its head removed, i.e., its head is completely erased, then since it is not an image but like an inanimate object, there is no karahah inside. The author of al-Hidayah said: An image without a head is not worshipped. So this is the way it is. ... Like an idol or lamp placed... [page 161] Chapter: What Invalidates Prayer and What is Disliked in It. The reason for karahah in placing [an idol] in front was that it was worshipped. So when this reason is not found, there is no karahah. Some people said that praying with a candle or lamp in front is makruh, just as if there is a brazier with visible coals or flaming fire in front of the worshiper, it is makruh. But the preferred view (raajih) is that there is no karahah.
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage contains two distinct rulings. First, an image that is decapitated (head erased) is not legally considered an image (timthal) because the head is essential for veneration; without it, it is like any inanimate object, and thus there is no karahah in its presence. This is based on the principle that karahah stems from respect or worship, which does not apply to a headless figure. Second, regarding praying facing a candle or lamp: some early scholars considered it makruh by analogy to fire-worship, but the preferred Hanafi view (the raajih qawl of later authorities) is that it is not makruh because the effective cause (worship) is absent—candles and lamps are not objects of worship. The commentary emphasizes that karahah is tied to the presence of worship (ibadah) of the object, not mere existence.

Key Terms
التمثال مقطوع الرأس (al-timthal maqtu' al-ra's): An image that is decapitated or whose head is erased. This is not legally considered an image and thus does not incur karahah.
عدم الكراهة ('adam al-karahah): Absence of dislike; the ruling that an action is permissible and not makruh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on an image that has its head erased?
A) It is still considered an image and prayer with it present is makruh.
B) It is not considered an image legally, so there is no karahah.
C) It is haram to keep such an image.
D) It invalidates prayer entirely.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school ties karahah to the object being an object of worship; hence, a decapitated image and a lamp do not incur karahah in prayer.

Ruling on Images in Prayer: Venerated vs. Disrespected
Ruling on images during prayer with distinction of veneration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on images in prayer based on the image's placement and posture, and rank the positions by severity of karahah.

Core Idea
If the image is stepped on or disrespected, prayer is not makruh; if venerated, it is makruh tanzih.

The Hanafi school provides a nuanced ruling regarding images during prayer, focusing on whether the image is treated with respect or contempt. This lesson clarifies when an image becomes makruh and ranks the positions relative to the worshiper, based on the classical text of al-Hidayah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The ruling differentiates between an image on a laid cushion or spread carpet (trampled/disrespected) and an image on an upright cushion or curtain (venerated).
The key distinction is ta'zim (veneration) vs. ihana (disrespect).
2
Understand the effective cause (illah)
Karahah arises from ta'zim. If the image is placed where it is stepped on (mudas wa mawtu'), there is no ta'zim, so no karahah.
The Hanafi school uses the concept of ta'zim as the effective cause.
3
Apply the ruling to the two scenarios
For laid cushions/carpets: prayer is not makruh (mubah). For upright cushions/curtains: prayer is makruh tanzih.
The karahah is tanzihi (disliked), not tahrimi (prohibited).
4
Learn the ranking of positions
The most severe karahah is when the image is in front of the worshiper, then above, then to the right, then to the left, then behind.
Some scholars say behind is not makruh for the prayer but still disliked in the house.
5
Note the exception and supporting anecdote
The anecdote of Hasan al-Basri and Ata illustrates that sitting on a cushion with an image is a sign of disrespect, hence permissible.
This reinforces the principle of disrespect (ihana) removing karahah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تصویر پڑے تکیے یا بچھونے پر ہو تو نماز مکروہ نہیں
ولو كانت الصورة على وسادة ملقاة او على بساط مفروش لا يكرة لانها تداس و توطأ بخلاف ما اذاك الوسادة منصوبة او كانت على الستر لانه تعظيم لها واشدها كراهة ان تكون امام المصلى ثم من فوق ثم على يمينه ثم على شماله ثم خلفه
ترجمہ اور اگر تصویر پڑے ہوئے تکیہ پر ہو یا بچھے ہوئے پچھونے پر تو مکروہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ تکیہ اور بچھونا وندا اور بچھایا جاتا ہے۔ اس کے جب کہ تکیہ کھڑا ہو یا تصویر پردہ پر ہو ۔ کیونکہ یہ تصویر کی تعظیم ہے۔ اور سب سے زیادہ کر بہت یہ ہے کہ تصویر مصلی کے را پھر یہ کہ مصلی کے سر کے اوپر ہو۔ پھر یہ کہ مصلی کے دائیں ہو پھر اس کے بائیں ہو پھر اس کے پیچھے ہو ۔ تشریح مسئلہ، اگر تصویر پڑے ہوئے تکیہ یا بچھے ہوئے بچھونے پر ہو تو یہ مکروہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ تکیہ اس حالت میں روندا جاتا ہے بچھایا جاتا ہے اور ظاہر ہے کہ اس صورت میں تصویر کی توہین اور تذلیل ہوگی نہ کی تعظیم ، چنانچہ اس کی تائید ایک حکایت سے بھی ہے حکایت یہ ہے کہ ایک دفعہ حسن بصری اور عطا ایک ایسے مکان میں داخل ہوئے جس میں ایک بچھونے پر تصویر میں تھیں پیس تھا۔ ہو گئے اور حسن بصری اس پر بیٹھ گئے۔ حضرت حسن بصری نے کہا کہ تصویر کی تعظیم اس پر نہ بیٹھنے میں ہے۔ ہاں اگر تکیہ کھڑا ہو اپنی پر ہو تو مکروہ ہے کیونکہ یہ تصویر کی تعظیم ہے یعنی کوئی بے تعظیمی اس کے ساتھ نہیں ہے۔
واشــد هـاكـراه ..... الخ سے اس بات کا بیان ہے کہ کراہت کے احادو افراد شدت و ضعف کے اعتبار سے مختلف : سب سے زیادہ کراہت اس میں ہے کہ تصویر مصلی کے آگے ہو پھر اس سے کم اس میں ہے کہ تصویر مصلی کے سر کے اوپر ہو پھر اک سے کہ مصلی کے دائیں ہو پھر یہ کہ بائیں ہو پھر یہ کہ مصلی کے پیچھے ہو ۔ بعض علماء نے کہا ہے کہ اگر تصویر مصلی کے پیچھے ہوتو نماز مکروی لیکن اس کا گھر میں ہونا مکروہ ہے کیونکہ نماز کی جگہ کو ایسی چیزوں سے پاک کرنا جو د خول ملائکہ سے مانع ہوں مستحب ہے۔
If the image is on a thrown cushion or a spread carpet, it is not makruh because it is stepped on and trampled, as opposed to when the cushion is upright or it is on a curtain, because that is a veneration of it. And the most severe karahah is that the image is in front of the worshiper, then above him, then to his right, then to his left, then behind him. Translation: And if the image is on a laid pillow or a spread bedsheet, it is not makruh because the pillow and bedsheet are stepped on and spread. However, when the pillow is upright or the image is on a curtain, it is makruh because that is veneration. And the most severe karahah is that the image is in front of the worshiper, then that it is above his head, then to his right, then to his left, then behind him. Explanation of the issue: If the image is on a laid pillow or a spread bedsheet, it is not makruh because the pillow in that state is stepped on and spread, and obviously in that case the image is disrespected and humiliated, not venerated. This is supported by an anecdote: Once Hasan al-Basri and Ata entered a house where there was an image on a bed. They saw it, and Hasan al-Basri sat on it. He said: 'Veneration of the image is in not sitting on it.' However, if the pillow is upright or on its own, it is makruh because that is veneration of the image—i.e., there is no disrespect associated with it. The phrase 'and the most severe karahah' onwards explains that the various instances of karahah differ in intensity: the most severe is when the image is in front of the worshiper, then lesser when it is above his head, then to his right, then to his left, then behind him. Some scholars said that if the image is behind the worshiper, the prayer is not makruh, but having it in the house is makruh because it is recommended to cleanse the place of prayer from things that prevent the entry of angels.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage is a direct ruling from the matn of al-Hidayah, followed by a detailed commentary. It establishes a clear principle: the karahah of images during prayer depends on whether the image is treated with respect or disrespect. An image that is on a cushion or carpet that is laid down and thus stepped on is not makruh because it is being disrespected (muhana). However, if the cushion is upright or the image is on a curtain, it is treated with veneration (ta'zim), hence makruh. The second part provides a ranking of positions relative to the worshiper: the most severe is in front (because the worshiper faces it), then above (because it overshadows), then right, then left, then behind. Some scholars even hold that behind is not makruh for the prayer itself but is still makruh in the house. The anecdote of Hasan al-Basri sitting on a cushion with an image reinforces that sitting on it is a sign of disrespect, so it is permissible.

Key Terms
تداس و توطأ (tudasu wa tawta'u): It is stepped on and trampled. This indicates disrespect, so the image is not venerated, thus no karahah.
تعظيم (ta'zim): Veneration or honor shown to the image. If the image is placed in a way that shows respect (e.g., mounted on a wall or upright cushion), it is makruh.
توطين (tawtin): Stepping on or trampling; the opposite of ta'zim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, what is the ruling if a prayer is performed with an image on a cushion that is placed upright in front of the worshiper?
A) The prayer is invalid (batil).
B) The prayer is valid but makruh tanzih.
C) The prayer is valid and not makruh because the image is on a cushion.
D) The prayer is mustahabb.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on images in prayer depends on whether the image is venerated; if it is stepped on or trampled, it is not makruh, otherwise it is makruh tanzih, with the front being the most severe position.

Praying in Clothes with Images: Validity and Dislike
States the ruling on praying in clothes with images

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prayer in clothes with images and explain the reason for the dislike and the recommended action.

Core Idea
Prayer in clothes with images is valid but makruh; repetition is recommended, not obligatory.

We now address a practical scenario: what if a person prays while wearing a garment that has images? The matn gives a clear ruling: the prayer is valid but disliked (makruh), and it is recommended to repeat it in non-makruh attire. Let's unpack the reasoning behind the dislike and the conditions that keep the prayer valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is praying while wearing a garment with images. The ruling is makruh tanzih (slightly disliked, not haram). Note that the prayer itself is valid.
2
Understand the reason for karahah
The likeness to 'hamil al-sanam' (idol-carrier) is the cause of dislike. Even without intention to worship, the resemblance triggers karahah.
Hanafi uses this analogy; other schools may differ.
3
State the validity and recommendation
Validity is because all conditions (shurut) of prayer are met. The recommended action (i'ada) is to repeat the prayer in a non-makruh manner.
i'ada is mustahabb, not wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تصویر والے لباس میں نماز مکروہ ہے
و لو لبس ثوبا فيه تصاوير يكره لانه يشبه حامل الصنم و الصلوة جائزة في جميع ذلك لات شرائطها و اتعاد على وجه غير مكروه وهو الحكم في كل صلوة اذيت مع الكل
ترجمہ اور اگر ایسا کپڑا پہنا جس میں تصویریں ہوں تو مکروہ ہے کیونکہ بہت اٹھانے والے کے مشابہ ہے۔ رہی نماز توان صورتوں میں جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ شرائط نماز سب جمع ہیں۔ اور غیر مکر وہ طریقہ پر نماز کا اعادہ کیا جائے اور یہی حکم ہبر اس نماز میں ہے
Prayer in clothes with images is makruh. And if one wears a garment in which there are images, it is makruh because it resembles the carrier of an idol. However, prayer is valid in all these cases because all its conditions are met. And the prayer should be repeated in a non-makruh manner. And this is the ruling for every prayer performed with dislike.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This is a final ruling from the matn. It addresses the scenario of a person praying while wearing clothes that have images (e.g., printed designs, logos, etc.). The karaahah is based on the likeness to an idol-carrier (hamil al-sanam), who carries an idol for worship. Even though the worshiper is not intending to worship the image, the external resemblance makes the prayer makruh tanzih. However, the prayer itself is valid because all essential conditions (taharah, facing qiblah, proper rukn, etc.) are fulfilled. The recommended action is to repeat the prayer in clothes without images. This ruling applies generally to any prayer performed while there is an element of karahah present (as in previous lessons). The phrase 'wa huwa al-hukm fi kulli salatin adaytuha ma'a al-kalah' indicates that for any prayer performed with karahah, it is valid but should be repeated.

Key Terms
حامل الصنم (hamil al-sanam): One who carries an idol, as done by idol-worshippers. Wearing clothes with images resembles this act, hence karahah.
اعادة (i'ada): Repetition of the prayer in a non-makruh manner. This is mustahabb (recommended), not wajib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person prays in a garment with images, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The prayer is invalid (batil) because of the presence of images.
B) The prayer is valid but makruh, and it is recommended to repeat it.
C) The prayer is valid and not makruh as long as the images are not worshipped.
D) The prayer is haram.

Key Takeaway
Prayer in clothes with images is valid but makruh tanzih; repeating the prayer in non-makruh attire is recommended but not obligatory.

Ruling on Images on Pillows and Bedding in Prayer
Clarifies when images on soft furnishings are not makruh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on images on floor furnishings during prayer and identify the condition (veneration) that determines dislike.

Core Idea
Images on floor coverings are not disliked in prayer; only images displayed with veneration are makruh.

This lesson examines a nuanced ruling from Al-Hidayah regarding images in the prayer area. While some may assume any image invalidates or disfavors the prayer, the Hanafi school distinguishes based on the treatment of the image. We will explore the key distinction between images that are stepped on (not makruh) and those that are honored (makruh), and the hierarchy of severity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what exactly is being ruled upon: the presence of an image on a pillow or mat during prayer. Note the two scenarios: lying down (not disliked) and upright (disliked).
2
Locate the condition for dislike
The decisive factor is veneration (تعظيم). If the image is displayed in a manner that honors it (upright, on curtain), it is makruh. If it is stepped on (floor covering), it is not.
The condition is based on the treatment of the image, not its mere existence.
3
Understand the basis from Hasan al-Basri's story
The text supports the ruling with the story of Hasan al-Basri who sat on a mat with images, stating that not sitting would be a form of veneration. This shows that stepping on images negates veneration.
This is a proof (dalil aqli) from the practice of a tabi'i.
4
Analyze the hierarchy of dislike
When the image is venerated, the severity of karaha depends on its position relative to the worshiper: front (most severe) > above > right > left > behind.
Some scholars extend karaha even to behind, but the relied-upon view restricts it to the positions listed.
5
Recognize the ikhtilaf
Some earlier scholars (e.g., Ata) considered it makruh to sit on such mats, but the Hanafi madhhab follows Hasan al-Basri's action as evidence for non-karahah.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the broader tradition.

Source Text

واشــد هـاكـراه ..... الخ سے اس بات کا بیان ہے کہ کراہت کے احادو افراد شدت و ضعف کے اعتبار سے مختلف : سب سے زیادہ کراہت اس میں ہے کہ تصویر مصلی کے آگے ہو پھر اس سے کم اس میں ہے کہ تصویر مصلی کے سر کے اوپر ہو پھر اک سے کہ مصلی کے دائیں ہو پھر یہ کہ بائیں ہو پھر یہ کہ مصلی کے پیچھے ہو ۔ بعض علماء نے کہا ہے کہ اگر تصویر مصلی کے پیچھے ہوتو نماز مکروی لیکن اس کا گھر میں ہونا مکروہ ہے کیونکہ نماز کی جگہ کو ایسی چیزوں سے پاک کرنا جو د خول ملائکہ سے مانع ہوں مستحب ہے۔
And if the image is on a pillow that is lying down or on a spread-out mat, it is not disliked because it is trod upon and stepped on. Unlike if the pillow is upright or the image is on a curtain, because that is a veneration of it. And the most severe dislike is if the image is in front of the worshiper, then above him, then to his right, then to his left, then behind him.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage from Al-Hidayah discusses the ruling of images (taswir) in the prayer area. The core principle is that images which are treated disrespectfully (by being sat or stepped on) are not makruh, because they are not being venerated. The dislike (karaha) attaches only when the image is displayed in a manner of honor—upright on a pillow, hanging on a curtain, or positioned relative to the worshiper in decreasing order: in front (most severe), above, right, left, behind. The commentary supports this with the story of Hasan al-Basri and Ata, where Hasan sat on a prayer mat with images, stating that not sitting would be a form of veneration. Some scholars extend the ruling to include that even having an image behind the worshiper is not makruh in prayer, but keeping it in the house is disliked because it may hinder angels. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that such images are not makruh if they are on the floor or bedding.

Key Terms
وسادة (wisada): A pillow or cushion that is typically placed on the floor for sitting or sleeping.
كراهة (karaha): Dislike, a legal category between prohibition and permissibility. In Hanafi fiqh, it includes tanzihi (slightly disliked) and tahrimi (prohibited-like).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, when is an image on a pillow considered makruh in prayer?
A) When the pillow is lying flat on the floor
B) When the pillow is placed upright
C) When the image is of a living being
D) Always makruh

Key Takeaway
Images on floor coverings are not disliked in prayer; only images displayed with veneration are makruh, with the severest being in front of the worshiper.

Wearing Image-Bearing Clothes in Prayer: Ruling and Distinction of Karaha
States ruling on wearing image-bearing clothes in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying in clothes with images and distinguish between the consequences of makruh tahrimi and makruh tanzihi.

Core Idea
Wearing clothes with images is makruh, but prayer is valid; repetition depends on type of karaha.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a common concern: what if someone prays while wearing a garment that has pictures? The ruling is clear but nuanced. The prayer itself is valid, but the act is disliked. Later Hanafi scholarship refined this by distinguishing between the level of dislike, which determines whether repetition is obligatory or recommended.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is wearing a garment that contains images (tasawir). The ruling from the text: it is makruh (disliked), but the prayer performed while wearing it is valid (ja'iz) because all conditions of prayer are fulfilled.
The reason for karaha is resemblance to idol-carriers (حامل الصنم).
2
Understand the recommendation for repetition
The author of Al-Hidayah recommends repeating the prayer in a non-disliked manner as a precaution (ihtiyat). This implies that while the prayer is valid, it is better to repeat it.
This recommendation is not a requirement in the original text.
3
Distinguish the types of karaha from later commentary
Fath al-Qadir (Ibn al-Humam) explains that the type of karaha determines the ruling on repetition: if the image is such that wearing it incurs makruh tahrimi (prohibitive dislike), then repetition is wajib; if only makruh tanzihi (slight dislike), repetition is mustahabb.
The distinction is based on the prominence and nature of the image.
4
Apply the distinction
For example, a large prominent image of a living being likely incurs makruh tahrimi, making repetition wajib. A small or non-prominent image may incur only makruh tanzihi, making repetition mustahabb.
This nuance is the mufta bihi position according to later Hanafi authorities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و لو لبس ثوبا فيه تصاوير يكره لانه يشبه حامل الصنم و الصلوة جائزة في جميع ذلك لات شرائطها و اتعاد على وجه غير مكروه وهو الحكم في كل صلوة اذيت مع الكل
ترجمہ اور اگر ایسا کپڑا پہنا جس میں تصویریں ہوں تو مکروہ ہے کیونکہ بہت اٹھانے والے کے مشابہ ہے۔ رہی نماز توان صورتوں میں جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ شرائط نماز سب جمع ہیں۔ اور غیر مکر وہ طریقہ پر نماز کا اعادہ کیا جائے اور یہی حکم ہبر اس نماز میں ہے
تشریح ایسا کپڑا پہنا جس میں تصویر میں ہوں مکروہ ہے کیونکہ یہ شخص بت اٹھانے والے کے مشابہ ہے۔ شبہ اس لئے کہا گیا کہ کپڑے میں واقعتہ بہت نہیں ۔
صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ ان سب مکر وہ صورتوں میں نماز جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ نماز کی تمام شرطیں جمع ہیں۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ نماز اگر مگر وہ طریقہ پر ادا کی گئی ہو تو احتیاط کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ اس کو غیر مکروہ طریقہ پر لوٹا یا جائے۔ شیخ قوام الدین کاکی نے شرح منار میں واجب کے لفظ کی تصریح فرمائی ہے یعنی نماز اگر مع الکراہت ادا ہوئی تو اس کا اعادہ واجب ہے۔ لیکن سچی ات یہ ہے کہ نماز اگر کراہت تحریمی کے ساتھ ادا کی گئی ہو تو اس کا اعادہ واجب ہے کیونکہ مکروہ تحریمی واجب کے مرتبہ میں ہوتا ہے اور اگر کراہت تنزیہیں کے ساتھ ادا کی گئی ہو تو اس کا اعادہ مستحب ہے۔ کیونکہ مکر و منہ ہی منتخب کے مرتبہ میں ہوتا ہے۔ (فتح القدیر)
And if one wears a garment in which there are images, it is disliked because it resembles the carrier of an idol. And the prayer is valid in all that because its conditions are fulfilled. And its repetition is on a non-disliked manner, and this is the ruling for every prayer performed with dislike.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling of praying while wearing clothes that have images (tasawir). The act of wearing such clothes is considered makruh (disliked) because it resembles polytheists who carry idols. However, the prayer itself remains valid (ja'iz) since all conditions of prayer are met. The text from Al-Hidayah recommends repeating the prayer in a non-disliked manner as a precaution (ihtiyat). The commentary by Ashraf Ul Hadaya (based on Fath al-Qadir) clarifies the type of repetition: if the prayer was performed with makruh tahrimi (prohibitive dislike), repetition is wajib (obligatory) because makruh tahrimi is equivalent to wajib in rank; if with makruh tanzihi (slight dislike), repetition is mustahabb (recommended). This distinction is crucial for understanding the legal consequences.

Key Terms
ثوب فيه تصاوير (thawb fihi tasawir): A garment that has pictures of living beings (animals, humans) printed or woven into it.
كراهة تحریمي (karaha tahrimi): Prohibitive dislike: an act which is not haram but is close to haram; its avoidance is obligatory (wajib).
كراهة تنزیهي (karaha tanzihi): Slight dislike: an act that is better to avoid but not sinful; its avoidance is recommended (mustahabb).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If one prays while wearing a shirt with a picture of a lion, what is the ruling on the prayer?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated
B) The prayer is valid but disliked (makruh)
C) The prayer is valid and not disliked
D) The prayer is invalid and cannot be repeated

Key Takeaway
The prayer is valid albeit disliked; whether repetition is wajib or mustahabb depends on the severity of the dislike (tahrimi vs. tanzihi).

Images of Inanimate Objects in Prayer
Clarifies that images of non-living things are not disliked in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on images of non-living things in prayer and explain the reason for the distinction between living and non-living subjects.

Core Idea
Images of non-living things are not disliked in prayer because they are not worshipped.

In Hanafi fiqh, the presence of images in prayer is a nuanced issue. While images of living beings may be disliked, this brief passage clarifies that images of inanimate objects—like mountains or trees—are perfectly permissible. The key principle is that dislike (karaha) is tied to the potential for veneration or worship. Let's examine how this ruling is derived and what it means for your prayer space.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject of the ruling
The passage mentions 'an image of a non-living thing' (تمثال غير ذي الروح). Determine what qualifies as non-living: plants, rocks, celestial bodies, buildings, etc.
Non-living means without a soul (rūḥ) in the Islamic context.
2
State the legal ruling
The text says such an image is 'not disliked' (لا يكره). This means it is permissible (mubah) and does not affect the validity or merit of prayer.
This is a straightforward ruling with no exceptions.
3
Analyze the reason ('illah)
The reason given is 'because it is not worshipped' (لانه لا يعبد). Dislike only arises when the image could be an object of veneration or idolatry. Inanimate objects are not typically worshipped.
This connects to the broader Hanafi principle that karaha is tied to reverence (ta'zim).
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a prayer room with a painting of a mountain. Since a mountain is non-living and not worshipped, the prayer is valid and not disliked.
This shows the practical application of the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يكرة تمثال غير ذي الروح لانه لا يعبد
ترجمہ اور غیر ذی روح کی تصویر مکروہ نہیں کیونکہ اس کی پرستش نہیں کی جاتی۔
تشریح واضح ہے۔
And an image of a non-living thing is not disliked because it is not worshipped.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This brief passage establishes a key principle in Hanafi fiqh regarding images (taswir) in prayer. The dislike (karaha) associated with images is specifically tied to the worship of them (ta'abbud). Images of inanimate objects (ghayr dhi al-ruh) such as trees, rocks, or mountains are not objects of worship and thus are not makruh. The commentary (تشریح) simply notes that this is clear. This ruling aligns with the earlier distinction: only images that are potentially venerated or resemble objects of idolatry cause dislike.

Key Terms
غير ذي الروح (ghayr dhi al-ruh): A being without a soul/rūḥ; inanimate objects, plants, and non-living things.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because they are not worshipped
C) Because they are not detailed
D) Because they are not colorful

Key Takeaway
Images of inanimate objects are permissible in prayer because the dislike is tied to the potential for worship, which inanimates do not attract.

Killing Snakes and Scorpions During Prayer
Permits killing dangerous animals during prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on killing harmful animals during prayer, cite the primary hadith evidence, and explain the rational basis for the ruling.

Core Idea
Killing a snake or scorpion during prayer is permissible and recommended because the Prophet's explicit command overrides the normal prohibition of excessive movement.

A worshiper in prayer may encounter a snake or scorpion that poses danger or distraction. Does this break the prayer? The Hanafi school, relying on a clear hadith and rational analogy, permits killing such creatures during prayer. This lesson examines the evidence and reasoning behind this exceptional ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
First, identify the specific act being ruled upon: killing a snake (hayyah) or scorpion ('aqrab) during prayer (salat). Then state the ruling: this act is permissible (mubah) and even recommended if the creature threatens or distracts.
The ruling applies to both snakes and scorpions; the hadith uses the term 'al-aswadayn' (the two black ones).
2
Locate the Primary Dalil (Evidence)
Find the primary proof: the hadith 'اقتلوا الاسودين ولو كنتم في الصلاة' (Kill the two black ones even if you are in prayer). This is a prophetic command (amr) that is explicit and overriding.
The hadith is classified as Sunnah ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is decisive (qat'i al-dalalah) in the Hanafi view.
3
Analyze the Wajh al-Dalalah (How the Dalil Proves the Ruling)
Examine how the hadith yields the ruling. The imperative 'اقتلوا' (kill) indicates permissibility and even recommendation (wujub is not intended because of other evidence). The phrase 'ولو كنتم في الصلاة' removes the normal restriction of moving during prayer.
Hanafi usul holds that the amr (imperative) usually indicates wujub, but here it is interpreted as ibahah because of the context of prayer and potential distraction.
4
Consider the Rational Argument (Ta'lil)
The text also provides a rational basis: killing the animal removes distraction (shughl) from the heart and allows khushu', analogous to pushing away a passerby (daf' al-marr). This strengthens the ruling by showing its wisdom.
This qiyas (analogy) is based on the common illah of removing something that disrupts prayer.
5
Note the Scope and Any Differences
The text clarifies that all types of snakes are included (yastawi jami' anwa' al-hayat) because the hadith is absolute (mutlaq). Other schools agree on permissibility but may differ on whether multiple blows invalidate the prayer. The Hanafi view is that even multiple movements do not invalidate as long as they are for this purpose.
The author of al-Hidayah did not specify one blow vs. multiple, implying that any necessary action is allowed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا بأس بقتل الحية والعقرب فى الصلوة لقوله عليه السلام اقتلوا الاسودين ولو كنتم في الصلوة ولان فيه لة الشغل فاشبه درء المار ويستوى جميع انواع الحيات هو الصحيح لا طلاق ماروينا جمہ اور سانپ اور بچھو کو نماز کے اندر مارنے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ حضور نے فرمایا کہ مل کرو تم دونوں کالوں کو ( سانپ جو) اگر چہ تم نماز میں ہو۔ اور اس لئے کہ اس میں دل کو مشغولیت کا دور کرتا ہے پس گزرنے والے کو دفع کرنے کے مشابہ ہو گیا۔ اور عمرمیں سانپ کی تمام متمیں داخل ہیں۔ یہی صحیح ہے اس حدیث کے مطلق ہونے کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے روایت کی ہے۔ ی نماز کی حالت میں سانپ اور بچھو کوقتل کرنا بلا کراہت مباح ہے دلیل حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا ارشادگرامی ہے (اقتلوا الاسودين کنم فی الصلوۃ) حدیث میں اسودین سے مراد سانپ اور بچھو ہیں۔ ترجمہ ہوا کہ سانپ اور بچھو کو مار ڈالو اگر چہ تم نماز میں ہو۔ اور نقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ سانپ اور بچھو کو مارنا اس وجہ سے جائز ہے کہ اس میں دل کا مشغول ہونا دور ہوتا ہے یعنی نمازی کی نظر جب تک بز کی رہے گی تو اس کا دل اسی طرف متوجہ رہے گتا اور نماز کی روح حضور قلب اس کو حاصل نہ ہو سکے گا۔ اس لئے کہا گیا کہ اس کو مار یال کی مشغولیت ختم ہو جائے اور حضور قلب نصیب ہو جائے۔ پس یہ سانپ اور بچھو کو مارنا نمازی کے آگے سے گزرنے والے کو دفع نے کے مشابہ ہو گیا۔ صاحب عنایہ نے لکھا ہے کہ مصنف ہدایہ نے اس کی کوئی تفصیل ذکر نہیں کی کہ ایک بار مار کر اس کو قتل کرے یا چند بار مارنے کی
There is no harm in killing a snake and a scorpion during prayer because of his statement (peace be upon him): 'Kill the two black ones even if you are in prayer.' And because it removes distraction, so it resembles pushing away a passerby. And all kinds of snakes are equal; this is the correct view due to the absoluteness of the hadith we narrated.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses the permissibility of killing a snake (hayyah) or scorpion ('aqrab) during prayer. The primary evidence is the hadith of the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wasallam): 'Kill the two black ones (al-aswadayn) even if you are in prayer' — referring to the snake and scorpion. The commentary provides an additional rational argument: the presence of such a dangerous creature distracts the heart from khushu' (presence of mind), so killing it removes the distraction and is analogous to pushing away someone who passes in front of the worshiper (daf' al-marr). The text explicitly states that all types of snakes are included in this ruling (yastawi jami' anwa' al-hayat), and this is the sahih (correct) view because the hadith is absolute (mutlaq). The commentary from Ashraf Ul Hadaya notes that al-`Ayni (in al-Binaya) remarked that the author of al-Hidayah did not specify whether the snake should be killed with one blow or multiple blows, implying that any means necessary is permitted.

Key Terms
الاسودين (al-aswadayn): Literally 'the two black ones'; in the hadith, it refers to the snake and scorpion, as they are commonly black in the Arabian context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Killing a snake or scorpion during prayer is permissible (mubah) based on the Prophet's explicit command and the removal of distraction.

Ruling on Wearing Clothing with Images in Prayer
Ruling on clothing with images and repetition due to karahah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wearing clothing with images during prayer and distinguish between images of living and non-living beings.

Core Idea
Wearing clothing with images of living beings is makruh tanzihi; prayer is valid but repetition is not required.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on wearing garments containing pictures during salah. We will see why such clothing is disliked (karahah) and how the type of image affects the ruling, based on the commentary in Ashraf al-Hidayah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is wearing clothing with images during prayer. The ruling is that it is makruh (disliked), but the prayer is still valid because all conditions are present.
2
Understand the reasoning behind the dislike
The dislike is due to resemblance to idol worshippers who carry idols. However, this is only a resemblance because the image is not actually worshipped.
The Arabic uses 'shabah' (resemblance) to indicate it's not actual idolatry.
3
Distinguish between living and non-living images
Images of living beings (animals, humans) are disliked because they can be objects of worship. Images of non-living things (trees, mountains) are not disliked at all, as confirmed by the text: 'And images of non-living beings are not disliked.'
The principle is that only what can be worshipped causes the dislike.
4
Confirm the validity of the prayer
Despite the dislike, the prayer is valid and does not need to be repeated solely due to this dislike, unless the dislike is of the tahrimi type (which this is not).
The text states: 'prayer is permissible because all conditions of prayer are present.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ما يفسد الصلوة وما يكره فيها تشریح ایسا کپڑا پہنا جس میں تصویر میں ہوں مکروہ ہے کیونکہ یہ شخص بت اٹھانے والے کے مشابہ ہے۔ شبہ اس لئے کہا گیا کہ کپڑے میں واقعتہ بہت نہیں ۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ ان سب مکر وہ صورتوں میں نماز جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ نماز کی تمام شرطیں جمع ہیں۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ نماز اگر مگر وہ طریقہ پر ادا کی گئی ہو تو احتیاط کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ اس کو غیر مکروہ طریقہ پر لوٹا یا جائے۔ شیخ قوام الدین کاکی نے شرح منار میں واجب کے لفظ کی تصریح فرمائی ہے یعنی نماز اگر مع الکراہت ادا ہوئی تو اس کا اعادہ واجب ہے۔ لیکن سچی ات یہ ہے کہ نماز اگر کراہت تحریمی کے ساتھ ادا کی گئی ہو تو اس کا اعادہ واجب ہے کیونکہ مکروہ تحریمی واجب کے مرتبہ میں ہوتا ہے اور اگر کراہت تنزیہیں کے ساتھ ادا کی گئی ہو تو اس کا اعادہ مستحب ہے۔ کیونکہ مکر و منہ ہی منتخب کے مرتبہ میں ہوتا ہے۔ (فتح القدیر) غیر ذی روح کی تصاویر مکروہ نہیں تشریح واضح ہے۔ ولا يكرة تمثال غير ذي الروح لانه لا يعبد ترجمہ اور غیر ذی روح کی تصویر مکروہ نہیں کیونکہ اس کی پرستش نہیں کی جاتی۔
Chapter on what invalidates prayer and what is disliked in it. Explanation: Wearing a garment with pictures is disliked because it resembles one who carries an idol. It is said 'resemblance' because the picture in the garment is not real. The author of Hidayah said that in all these disliked forms, prayer is permissible because all conditions of prayer are present. The author of Hidayah says that if prayer is performed in a disliked manner, caution demands that it be repeated in a non-disliked manner. Shaykh Qawam al-Din al-Kaki in Sharh al-Manar clarified the word 'wajib': meaning if prayer is performed with dislike, its repetition is wajib. But the truth is that if prayer is performed with makruh tahrimi, its repetition is wajib because makruh tahrimi is of the rank of wajib. And if performed with karahah tanzihiyyah, its repetition is mustahabb because makruh tanzihi is of the rank of mustahabb. (Fath al-Qadir) Images of non-living beings are not disliked. Explanation is clear. And images of non-living beings are not disliked because they are not worshipped. Translation: And images of non-living beings are not disliked because they are not worshipped.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses two related rulings: the dislike (karahah) of wearing clothing with images during prayer, and the ruling on repeating a prayer performed with dislike. The author first explains that wearing a garment with pictures is makruh because it resembles idolatry, but the resemblance is only superficial since the image is not actually worshipped. The author of Hidayah (the original text) states that despite the dislike, the prayer is valid because all conditions are fulfilled. The commentary then introduces the precautionary repetition: if the prayer was performed with makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked), repetition is wajib (obligatory) because makruh tahrimi is at the level of wajib in terms of necessity. If it was performed with makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked), repetition is mustahabb (recommended). The passage also clarifies that images of non-living beings (e.g., trees, mountains) are not disliked at all because they are not objects of worship. This distinction is based on the principle that karahah in worship relates to resemblance of prohibited acts, and only living beings were historically worshipped.

Key Terms
مکروہ تحریمی (makruh tahrimi): An act that is prohibitively disliked, close to haram; in prayer it requires repetition.
مکروہ تنزیہی (makruh tanzihi): An act that is lightly disliked, close to mubah; repetition is recommended but not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The prayer is haram and must be repeated.

Key Takeaway
Images of living beings on clothing cause makruh tanzihi in prayer, but the prayer remains valid; non-living images are not disliked.

Repetition of Prayer Performed with Karahah: Tahrimi vs Tanzihi
Ruling on clothing with images and repetition due to karahah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between makruh tahrimi and makruh tanzihi and state the ruling on repeating a prayer performed with each type of dislike.

Core Idea
If prayer is performed with makruh tahrimi, repetition is wajib; with makruh tanzihi, repetition is mustahabb.

This lesson focuses on the Hanafi principle that not all disliked acts in prayer require the same remedy. The distinction between makruh tahrimi and makruh tanzihi determines whether repetition is obligatory or merely recommended, as clarified by later Hanafi authorities.

Guided Path
1
Recall the two categories of karahah in Hanafi fiqh
Karahah is divided into tahrimi (prohibitively disliked, close to haram) and tanzihi (lightly disliked, close to mubah). This classification is unique to the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the type of dislike for the act in question
The act here is wearing clothing with images. The text indicates it is makruh tanzihi. But the general principle can apply to any disliked act in prayer.
3
Apply the ruling based on the type of karahah
If the prayer was performed with makruh tahrimi, repetition is wajib (obligatory). If with makruh tanzihi, repetition is mustahabb (recommended). The text cites Fath al-Qadir for this distinction.
4
Understand the rationale: rank of the disliked act
Makruh tahrimi is of the rank of wajib in terms of necessity, so its violation requires repetition. Makruh tanzihi is of the rank of mustahabb, so repetition is not required but recommended for caution.

Chapter on what invalidates prayer and what is disliked in it. Explanation: Wearing a garment with pictures is disliked because it resembles one who carries an idol. It is said 'resemblance' because the picture in the garment is not real. The author of Hidayah said that in all these disliked forms, prayer is permissible because all conditions of prayer are present. The author of Hidayah says that if prayer is performed in a disliked manner, caution demands that it be repeated in a non-disliked manner. Shaykh Qawam al-Din al-Kaki in Sharh al-Manar clarified the word 'wajib': meaning if prayer is performed with dislike, its repetition is wajib. But the truth is that if prayer is performed with makruh tahrimi, its repetition is wajib because makruh tahrimi is of the rank of wajib. And if performed with karahah tanzihiyyah, its repetition is mustahabb because makruh tanzihi is of the rank of mustahabb. (Fath al-Qadir) Images of non-living beings are not disliked. Explanation is clear. And images of non-living beings are not disliked because they are not worshipped. Translation: And images of non-living beings are not disliked because they are not worshipped.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses two related rulings: the dislike (karahah) of wearing clothing with images during prayer, and the ruling on repeating a prayer performed with dislike. The author first explains that wearing a garment with pictures is makruh because it resembles idolatry, but the resemblance is only superficial since the image is not actually worshipped. The author of Hidayah (the original text) states that despite the dislike, the prayer is valid because all conditions are fulfilled. The commentary then introduces the precautionary repetition: if the prayer was performed with makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked), repetition is wajib (obligatory) because makruh tahrimi is at the level of wajib in terms of necessity. If it was performed with makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked), repetition is mustahabb (recommended). The passage also clarifies that images of non-living beings (e.g., trees, mountains) are not disliked at all because they are not objects of worship. This distinction is based on the principle that karahah in worship relates to resemblance of prohibited acts, and only living beings were historically worshipped.

Key Terms
مکروہ تحریمی (makruh tahrimi): An act that is prohibitively disliked, close to haram; in prayer it requires repetition.
مکروہ تنزیہی (makruh tanzihi): An act that is lightly disliked, close to mubah; repetition is recommended but not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling on repeating a prayer that was performed with makruh tahrimi?
A) Repetition is not required.
B) Repetition is mustahabb.
C) Repetition is wajib.
D) The prayer is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The obligation to repeat a prayer performed with karahah depends on the type: wajib for tahrimi, mustahabb for tanzihi.
