Killing Snakes and Scorpions During Prayer: A Rulings and Proof Analysis
Ruling with proof: killing snakes and scorpions during prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on killing harmful animals during prayer and explain why multiple strikes do not invalidate the prayer.

Core Idea
Killing a snake or scorpion during prayer is permissible, and even multiple strikes are rukhsah, not amal kathir.

The presence of a snake or scorpion during prayer naturally distracts the worshipper, undermining khushu'. The Hanafi school, drawing on a clear prophetic permission, rules that killing such creatures is not only allowed but removes the distraction. This lesson examines the textual proof, the analogical reasoning, and addresses the concern that multiple strikes might invalidate the prayer. We will also see how later Hanafi masters resolved an internal disagreement about white snakes.

Guided Path
1
State the core ruling and its basis
Identify the ruling (mubah) and the primary proof: the hadith 'Kill the two black ones even if you are in prayer.' Understand that the 'two black ones' (al-aswadayn) refer to the snake and scorpion, and the command is a special concession for prayer.
The ruling is not obligatory but permissible; the hadith overrides the general principle of avoiding unnecessary movement.
2
Analyse the hadith proof
Examine the imperative 'قتلوا' (kill). In Hanafi usul, a command indicates permission unless a qarina (context) shifts it to obligation. Here the phrase 'ولو كنتم في الصلاة' is a qarina allowing the act even during the prayer's usual restrictions.
The hadith's generality (عموم) covers all snakes and scorpions, regardless of color.
3
Trace the qiyas analogy
The commentary draws an analogy (qiyas) to warding off a passerby during prayer, which is also permitted. Both acts remove a source of distraction (شغل). The common cause (علة) is the removal of harm/distraction.
This is qiyas jaliy (clear analogy) because the illa is explicit in both cases.
4
Examine the amal kathir objection
Some jurists argue that multiple strikes constitute excessive action (amal kathir) which would normally invalidate prayer. The Hanafi response is that this is a special concession (rukhsah) from the Lawgiver, similar to the permission to fetch water and perform wudu after hadath during prayer.
The principle: a rukhsah can overrule the general rule of amal kathir.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute on white snakes
Faqih Abu Ja'far al-Hindwani reports a hadith forbidding killing white snakes as they are jinn. Imam al-Tahawi rejects this distinction, noting the Prophet's covenant with jinn forbids them from appearing as snakes; if they do, the covenant is broken. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi adopts Tahawi's view, and explains that 'al-aswadayn' in the hadith is a general Arab term for any harmful reptile.
The preferred view (mufta bihi) is that all snakes, regardless of color, may be killed and are not to be distinguished.

The ruling on killing harmful animals during prayer. There is no harm in killing a snake and scorpion in prayer due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'Kill the two black ones even if you are in prayer' and because it removes distraction, so it resembles warding off a passerby. All types of snakes are included; this is correct due to the absoluteness of the hadith we narrated. Meaning: Killing snake and scorpion in prayer is permissible without dislike. The proof is the hadith 'Kill the two black ones even in prayer'. The 'two black ones' refer to snake and scorpion. Translation: Kill the snake and scorpion even if you are in prayer. The textual proof is that killing them removes distraction; as long as the worshipper's gaze is on them, his heart is preoccupied and the spirit of prayer (presence of heart) is not attained. Therefore killing them ends distraction and attains presence of heart. So killing snake and scorpion resembles warding off a passerby. The author of Inayah wrote that the author of Hidayah did not mention detail whether to kill with one strike or multiple. On page 163: If needed, kill with several strikes. This is the opinion of Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi: if possible with one strike, do that; if multiple are needed, do not refrain. The goal is to kill, whether with one or many. The proof is that the Prophet said 'Kill the two black ones' and there is no detail. Some jurists thought that if one strike suffices, kill and do not repeat prayer; if multiple strikes needed, repeat prayer because it is excessive action (amal kathir) that invalidates. The response is that indeed multiple strikes are amal kathir, but this is a concession (rukhsah) from the Law, like after hadath, the worshipper fetching water and performing wudu—this is a collection of many actions but due to the Law's concession, it does not invalidate prayer. Similarly here there is a concession. So repeated striking does not invalidate. The author said that all types of snakes are included whether white, hairy, or black. This is correct because the hadith is absolute and includes all. Faqih Abu Ja'far al-Hindwani said that some white snakes that walk in houses are jinn, and killing them is not permissible because Allah's Messenger said: 'Beware of killing white snakes, for they are jinn.' The hadith makes no distinction between prayer and non-prayer, so that type of snake cannot be killed even outside prayer, unless first warned: 'Go away, lest we kill you', then if it does not go, killing becomes permitted. Imam Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi said that distinguishing between snakes is wrong because the Prophet took a covenant from jinn that they would not appear in the form of snakes or enter their houses. So when they break the covenant, their killing becomes permissible. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi adopted this view, and in the hadith 'al-aswadayn' does not mean black snakes specifically; rather it is used in Arab custom to mean absolute, whatever the color.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents a detailed discussion on killing harmful animals (snakes and scorpions) during prayer. The core ruling is that it is permissible without any dislike (bila karahah) based on the prophetic hadith 'اقتلوا الاسودين ولو كنتم في الصلاة' (Kill the two black ones even if you are in prayer). The two black ones (al-aswadayn) refers to the snake and scorpion. The rationale is that the presence of such creatures distracts the heart from khushu' (presence of mind), which is the essence of prayer. Killing them removes this distraction and is analogous to repelling something that passes in front of the worshipper. The commentary addresses a key ikhtilaf: some jurists argue that if multiple strikes are needed, it constitutes amal kathir (excessive action) which invalidates prayer. However, the Hanafi response is that although multiple strikes are amal kathir, it is permitted by a specific concession (rukhsah) from the Shari'ah, similar to the permission for a person who becomes impure during prayer to go fetch water and perform wudu, which also involves many actions. Therefore, the prayer remains valid even with multiple strikes. The passage also includes a intra-Hanafi dispute regarding white snakes: Abu Ja'far al-Hindwani reported a hadith forbidding killing white snakes because they are jinn, so killing them is not permissible at all, whether in prayer or not, unless after warning. Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi rejects this distinction, noting that the covenant with jinn prohibits them from appearing as snakes; if they do, they break the covenant and can be killed. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi adopts Tahawi's view, and explains that 'al-aswadayn' in the hadith is not limited to black snakes but is a general term in Arab custom for snakes of any color. The Hanafi position is that all snakes, regardless of color, may be killed during prayer, and the prayer remains valid.

Key Terms
عمل کثیر (amal kathir): Excessive action that normally invalidates prayer; here exempted due to necessity and specific permission.
اسودین (al-aswadayn): The two black ones: refers to snake and scorpion in the hadith; in Arab custom it is general for harmful creatures regardless of color.
رخصت (rukhsah): A special concession from the Lawgiver that allows an act that would otherwise be prohibited or invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following best describes the Hanafi ruling on killing a snake with multiple strikes during prayer?
A) The prayer is invalidated because three or more strikes constitute amal kathir.
B) The prayer remains valid because the Lawgiver has granted a special concession (rukhsah).
C) The prayer is valid only if the snake is black, not if it is white.
D) The prayer is valid only if the strike occurs between the prostrations.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits killing harmful animals (snakes, scorpions) during prayer, with multiple strikes validated by a special concession, and all types of snakes are included without distinction.

Counting Verses and Tasbihat During Prayer
Ruling on counting verses/tasbihat with fingers during prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on counting verses/tasbihat with fingers during prayer and distinguish between the primary view and the Sahibayn's view.

Core Idea
Counting with the hand during prayer is makruh because it is not from the actions of prayer, though the Sahibayn permit it to ensure correct recitation.

In prayer, our focus should be on the acts of worship as prescribed by the Sunnah. One common distraction is counting the number of verses or tasbihat (glorifications) with the fingers. The Hanafi school addresses this with a clear ruling: it is disliked (makruh tanzihi). However, this ruling is nuanced by a difference of opinion within the school itself, as the two foremost students of Imam Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, deem it permissible. This lesson will unpack the reasoning behind each view and establish the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the specific action being assessed and its legal classification: counting verses or tasbihat with the hand during prayer, which is ruled as makruh (disliked).
The ruling applies to both obligatory and supererogatory prayers.
2
Understand the dalil (evidence)
The primary evidence is that such counting is not from the actions of prayer (laysa min a'mal al-salah). Any extra movement not part of the prayer's prescribed acts is discouraged.
The dalil is based on the general principle that actions outside the prayer are disliked unless specifically permitted.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Recognize that the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) see no harm (la ba'sa) in counting during prayer, citing the need to observe the sunnah of correct recitation.
Their view is a valid ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school, based on a different prioritization of sunnah observance.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The response to the Sahibayn is that the worshipper can count the required number before starting the prayer, thereby eliminating the need to count during it.
This preserves the disliked nature of counting during prayer by offering an alternative.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is the primary view that it is makruh tanzihi, as the majority and the text of the Hidayah adopt it.
The Sahibayn's view is acknowledged but not preferred for practice.

و يكره عد الاى والتسبيحات باليد في الصلوة و كذلك عد السور لان ذلك ليس من اعمال النار وعن ابى يوسف ومحمد انه لابأس بذلك فى الفرائض والنوافل جميعا مراعاة لسنة القراءة والم بماجاءت به السنة قلنا يمكنه ان يعد ذلك قبل الشروع فيستغنى عن العد بعده والنا ترجمہ اور نماز کے اندر ہاتھ کے ذریعہ تسبیحات اور آیات کو شمار کرنا مکروہ ہے اور یہی حکم سورتوں کے شمار کرنے کا ہے کیونکہ بار اعمال میں سے نہیں ہے اور صاحبین سے مروی ہے کہ اس کا کوئی مضائقہ نہیں فرائض اور نوافل میں سعیت قراءت کی رعایت کرنے اور اس چیز پر عمل کرنے کی وجہ سے جو سنت میں آئی ہے ہم جواب دیتے ہیں مصلی کے لئے ممکن ہے کہ اس کو شروع نماز سے پہیے ؟ تو اس کے بعد شمار کرنے سے مستفی ہوگا۔ واللہ اعلم تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ نماز کے اندر ہاتھ کے ذریعہ تسبیحات اور آیتوں کا شمار کرنا مکروہ ہے نماز خواہ فرض خواہ نفل ، اسی طرن کا
And it is disliked to count verses and tasbihat with the hand in prayer, and likewise counting surahs, because that is not from the actions of prayer. From Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: There is no harm in that in both obligatory and supererogatory prayers, out of consideration for the sunnah of recitation and acting upon what the sunnah has brought. We say: It is possible for the worshipper to count that before starting, so he becomes independent of counting afterwards. Translation: And counting tasbihat and verses with the hand during prayer is disliked, and the same ruling applies to counting surahs, because it is not from the actions of prayer. And from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: It is no problem in obligatory and supererogatory prayers, out of consideration for observing the sunnah of recitation and acting upon what has come in the sunnah. We respond: It is possible for the worshipper to count that before starting, so he will be independent of counting afterwards. And Allah knows best. Explanation: The issue is that counting tasbihat and verses with the hand during prayer is disliked, whether the prayer is obligatory or supererogatory.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on counting the number of verses or tasbihat (glorifications) with the fingers during prayer. The primary ruling is that it is makruh (disliked) because such counting is not part of the actions of prayer (laysa min a'mal al-salah). The author includes both obligatory (fara'id) and supererogatory (nawafil) prayers in this ruling. However, a concession is reported from the two disciples (al-Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani): they see no harm in it, based on the need to observe the sunnah of recitation correctly (e.g., ensuring one recites the required number of tasbihat in ruku' and sujud). The main text (Hidayah) responds to this by stating the worshipper can count the verses or tasbihat before starting the prayer, thus eliminating the need to count during prayer. The commentary affirms the disliked nature of counting during prayer, for both fard and nafl. This shows the Hanafi preference for avoiding unnecessary movements that distract from khushu'.

Key Terms
عد (adad): Counting (verses or tasbihat) with the hand during prayer; considered an unnecessary action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It is recommended (sunnah).
C) It is disliked (makruh tanzihi).
D) It is forbidden (haram).

Key Takeaway
Counting verses/tasbihat with fingers during prayer is makruh tanzihi because it is not part of the actions of prayer; one can count beforehand to avoid the dislike.

Killing a Snake in Prayer: Multiple Strikes and the Hanafi Ruling
Ruling on striking a snake multiple times in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on killing a snake during prayer with multiple strikes and explain the proof from hadith and the principle of istihsan.

Core Idea
Multiple strikes to kill a snake in prayer are permitted by Shari'ah license, not invalidating the prayer, based on the general command 'kill the two black ones'.

What happens if a snake appears while you are praying? Can you strike it multiple times, or would that invalidate your prayer? This lesson examines the Hanafi position on this scenario, focusing on the proof from the Prophet's command and the key principle of istihsan (juristic preference) that licenses necessary actions even if they are outwardly excessive.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the question
The passage considers a person in prayer who needs to kill a harmful snake. The question is whether striking multiple times (excessive action) invalidates the prayer.
The snake must be genuinely threatening; this is not about killing unnecessarily.
2
State the Hanafi position
According to Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi and adopted by the author, the prayer remains valid even if multiple strikes are needed. The objective is to kill the snake, whether by one strike or many.
This is the mufta bihi (operative) position.
3
Analyze the primary proof (dalil)
The Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded: 'Kill the two black ones' (the snake and the scorpion). This command is general (amm) with no restriction to one strike or to outside prayer. In Hanafi usul, a general command indicates permissibility (ibaha) in the absence of a restrictive text.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but sufficient for a non-obligatory ruling.
4
Understand the istihsan (juristic preference) argument
Critics say multiple strikes are 'amal kathir (excessive action) that normally invalidates prayer. The Hanafi response invokes istihsan: the Shari'ah itself grants a license for such necessity, just as it permits a person who encounters impurity in the mosque to fetch water and perform wudu—a series of actions that would otherwise be invalidating. Thus, the license overrides the general rule.
This is an example of istihsan overriding qiyas.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi disagreement and resolution
Some later Hanafi jurists held that if multiple strikes are needed, the prayer must be repeated because it becomes excessive. The author sides with Sarakhsi, and the passage also rejects distinctions between snake types (white vs. black), including all harmful snakes under the ruling.
The disagreement is resolved by adopting the view that the hadith's generality applies to all snakes, and the license covers all necessary actions.

باب ما يفسد الصلوة وما يكره فيها

ضرورت پیش آئے تو چند مرتبہ مار کر قتل کر دے یہی قول شمس الائمہ السرخسی کا ہے یعنی اگر ضرب واحد سے قتل کرنا ممکن ہو تو ایک نو کو عمل میں لائے اور اگر چند ضربوں کی ضرورت پڑے تو اس سے بھی دریغ نہ کرے۔ حاصل یہ کہ مقصود اس کو قتل کرنا ہے ایک ہانی سے ہو یا متعد دضر بوں سے ہو ۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اقتلوا الاسو دین فرمایا ہے اور اس میں کوئی تفصیل نہیں ہے۔ بعض فقہاء کا خیال یہ ہے کہ اگر ایک ضرب سے قتل کرنا ممکن ہو تو مار ڈالے اور نماز نہ اونا ئے۔ اور اگر متعد دضر میں عمل کر پر پڑیں تو نماز کا اعادہ کرے کیونکہ یہ عمل کثیر ہے اور عمل کثیر مفسد نساز ہے لیکن اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ بلاشبہ متعدد بار ڈنڈا مارے کثیر ہے لیکن یہ عمل کثیر ایسا ہے جس کی منجانب شرع رخصت اور اجازت ہے۔ جیسے نماز میں حدیث پیش آنے کے بعد مصلی کا پیڑ سے پانی کا نکالنا اور وضو کرنا یہ مجموعہ عمل کثیر ہے مگر شریعت کے رخصت دینے کی وجہ سے مفسد نماز نہیں ہے ، ایسے ہی یہاں کی شریعت کی طرف سے رخصت ہے۔ اس لئے بار بار مار نا مفسد نماز نہیں ہو گا۔ فاضل مصنف نے کہا کہ اس حکم میں سانپ کی تمام مقسمیں داخل ہیں خواہ وہ سفید ہو یا گیسودار ہو یا کا لانگ ہو۔ یہی قول سی نے جو حدیث ہم نے روایت کی ہے وہ مطلق ہے سب کو شامل ہے فقیہ ابو جعفر ہندوانی نے کہا بعض سانپ سفید رنگ کے گھروں میں ۔ سید ھے چلتے ہیں وہ جن ہوتے ہیں ان کو حل کرنا مباح نہیں۔ کیونکہ اللہ کے بچے رسول عالیہ السلام نے فرمایا۔ ایسا کم والحبتها فانها من الجن یعنی سفید رنگت کے سانپ کو قتل کرنے سے بچو اس لئے کہ وہ جن ہوتا ہے۔ حدیث میں نماز اور غیر نماز کی کوئی نہیں ہے لہذا اس قسم کے سانپ کو غیر نماز میں بھی مارنے کی اجازت نہیں ہے ہاں اگر پہلے یہ کہ دیا کہ تم چلے جاؤ مسلمانوں کاراست و
ور نہ ہم مارڈالیں گے اس کے باوجود بھی اگر وہ نہ جائے تو اس کو قتل کرنا مباح ہے۔
امام ابو جعفر طحاوی نے کہا کہ سانپوں کے درمیان فرق کرنا غلط ہے کیونکہ حضور نے نے جنات سے یہ عہد و پیمان لیا تھا کہ وہ امن سامنے سانپ کی صورت میں ظاہر نہ ہوں اور نہ ان کے گھروں میں گھسیں پس جب انہوں نے نقص عبد کیا تو ان کا قتل میان ہوگیا قول کو شمس الائمہ سرخسی نے اختیار کیا ہے اور حدیث میں اس دین سے مراد سیاہ سانپ نہیں بلکہ یہ نقط عرب کے عرف میں مطلقہ کے لئے بولا جاتا ہے خواہ کسی رنگ کا ہو۔
Chapter of what invalidates prayer and what is disliked therein. When need arises, he may kill [the snake] by striking several times. This is the saying of Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi. That is, if it is possible to kill with a single strike, he should do that; but if multiple strikes are needed, he should not refrain. The point is that the objective is to kill it, whether by one hand or multiple strikes. The proof is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Kill the two black ones' and there is no detail in it. Some jurists opine that if killing with one strike is possible, he should kill and not invalidate the prayer; but if multiple strikes are needed, he should repeat the prayer because it is excessive action, and excessive action invalidates. But the response to this is: Undoubtedly striking multiple times is excessive, but this excessive action is one for which there is license and permission from the Shari'ah. Just like after encountering a [hadath] in prayer, the one praying removes water from a container and performs wudu – this is a combination of excessive actions, but due to the Shari'ah's permission, it is not invalidating. Similarly, here there is license from the Shari'ah. Hence, striking repeatedly will not invalidate the prayer. The author [al-Marghinani] said: All kinds of snakes are included in this ruling, whether white, long-haired, or black. This is the saying of [the narrator of] the hadith we narrated, which is absolute and includes all. Faqih Abu Ja'far al-Hindwani said: Some white snakes that move about in houses are jinn; it is not permissible to kill them, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Beware of killing the white ones, for they are of the jinn.' The hadith makes no distinction between prayer and non-prayer. Hence, it is not permissible to kill this type even outside prayer. But if it is first warned, 'Leave, otherwise we will kill you,' and it still does not leave, then killing it becomes permissible. Imam Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi said that differentiating between snakes is wrong, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) took a covenant from the jinn that they would not appear in the form of snakes nor enter their homes. Then when they breached that, killing them became permissible. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi adopted this saying. And in the hadith, by 'the two black ones' is not meant black snakes; rather, in the custom of the Arabs, it is used for absolute [snakes], whatever their color.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school regarding killing a snake during prayer with multiple strikes. The author opens by stating the position of Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi: if a snake threatens during prayer, one may kill it with as many strikes as necessary; the prayer remains valid. The proof is the Prophet's command 'Kill the two black ones' (the snake and the scorpion), which is unconditional. Some jurists argue that multiple strikes constitute excessive action ('amal kathir) which invalidates prayer, and thus require repetition. The Hanafi response uses istihsan (juristic preference): this excessive action is permitted by Shari'ah due to necessity, just as removing water and performing wudu inside the mosque after a hadath is permitted despite being excessive. The passage then discusses the type of snake: the author (Marghinani in al-Hidayah) includes all snakes. Al-Hindwani distinguishes white snakes as jinn, citing a hadith to avoid killing them, but Tahawi and Sarakhsi reject this distinction, holding that all snakes can be killed if they are harmful, and the hadith 'kill the two black ones' is general. The Hanafi position is that killing a harmful snake in prayer is permitted regardless of color, and multiple strikes do not invalidate prayer due to Shari'ah's dispensation.

Key Terms
عمل کثیر (amal kathir): Excessive action that normally invalidates prayer, but here exempted due to Shari'ah license.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on killing a snake in prayer if multiple strikes are needed?
A) The prayer becomes invalid and must be repeated.
B) It is permissible and the prayer remains valid.
C) It is forbidden and the prayer must be repeated.
D) It is makruh but the prayer is valid.

Key Takeaway
Killing a harmful snake during prayer with multiple strikes is permitted and does not invalidate the prayer, based on the general command of the Prophet and the Shari'ah's license for necessity.

Counting Verses and Tasbihat with the Hand in Prayer
Ruling on counting verses/tasbihat with the hand during prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on counting with the hand in prayer, distinguish between the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and apply the distinctions between counting with the hand, finger joints, heart, and tongue.

Core Idea
Counting with the hand in prayer is makruh; counting with finger joints or heart is permissible; counting with the tongue invalidates the prayer.

This lesson examines a subtle but common issue in prayer: counting verses or tasbihat using the hand. While the Zahir al-Riwayah deems this makruh (disliked), the Sahibayn permit it in order to preserve the Sunnah of recitation. Understanding the exact means of counting is crucial to avoid invalidating the prayer and to follow the relied-upon position of the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the Zahir al-Riwayah ruling
Recognize that the act in question is counting verses, tasbihat, or surahs with the hand during prayer. The Zahir al-Riwayah states that this is makruh because it is not from the actions of prayer.
Makruh here is tanzihi (disliked but not sinful).
2
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) transmit a view that there is no harm in counting with the hand in both fard and nafl prayers, especially to observe the Sunnah recitation (e.g., reciting forty verses in Fajr).
This is a non-Zahir al-Riwayah transmission.
3
Understand Imam Abu Hanifa's response
Imam Abu Hanifa argues that the need to count can be fulfilled before beginning the prayer by planning the recitation. Therefore, counting during prayer is unnecessary and thus makruh.
This response addresses the Sahibayn's proof about Salat al-Tasbih and other sunnah practices.
4
Distinguish means of counting
The phrase 'with the hand' (bil-yad) implies that counting with finger joints, pressing joints, or by heart is not makruh. Counting with the tongue is considered speech and invalidates the prayer.
This distinction is crucial for practical application.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the Zahir al-Riwayah: counting with the hand in prayer is makruh. The Sahibayn's view, though transmitted, is not taken as operative.
The tarjih is supported by the author of al-Hidayah and the Urdu commentator.

۱۶۵
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد دوم باب ما يفسد الصلوة وما يكره فيها ثر کرنا بھی مکروہ ہے کیونکہ آیات یا تسبیحات یا سورتوں کا شمار کرنا نماز کے اعمال سے نہیں ہے یہی ظاہر الروایۃ ہے بالید کی قید سے معلوم ہوا کہ انگلیوں کے پوروں سے دبا کر یا دل سے یاد کرنا مکروہ نہیں ہے ۔ بالید کی قید سے یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ زبان سے شمار نہ کرے کیونکہ
زبان سے شمار کرنا مفسد نماز ہے۔
مصنف نے فی الصلواۃ کی قید ذکر کر کے اس طرف اشارہ کر دیا کہ غیر نماز کی صورت میں شمار کرنا مکروہ نہیں ہے لیکن علامہ فخر الاسلام نے ذکر کیا کہ خارج صلوۃ بھی تسبیح کا شمار کرنا بدعت ہے اور فرمایا و كان السلف يقولون نذنب ولاتخصى و نسبح و لحضی یعنی اسلاف کہتے تھے کہ ہم گناہ تو بے شمار کرتے ہیں اور اس کو شمار نہیں کرتے ، اور تسبیح پڑھتے ہیں تو شمار کرتے ہیں یہ غیر ظاہر الروایۃ میں صاحبین سے مروی ہے آیات یا تسبیحات کو فرائض اور نوافل دونوں میں شمار کرنے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ بسا اوقات انسان کو آیات شمار کرنے کی ضرورت پڑتی ہے مثلاً وہ چاہتا ہے کہ فرائض میں مسنون طریقہ پر قراءت کرے یعنی چالیس یا ساتھ آیات پڑھے جیسا کہ سنت رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم سے ثابت ہے یا مثلا صلوۃ التسبیح میں جس پر سنت وارد ہوئی ہے اس پر عمل کرنا چاہتا ہے۔ اب ظاہر ہے کہ ان دونوں صورتوں میں بغیر شمار کے کوئی چارہ کار نہیں ہے لہذا اس وقت شمار کرنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہوگا ۔ امام ابو خلیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قراءت مسنونہ پر عمل اس طور پر بھی ہو سکتا ہے کہ نماز شروع کرنے سے پہلے شمار کر کے متعین کرلے کہ پہلی رکعت میں یہاں سے یہاں تک پڑھوں گا اور دوسری میں یہاں سے یہاں تک پڑھوں گا پس اس صورت میں نماز میں شمار کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں رہے گی۔ رہا صلوۃ استیج کا کا معاملہ تو اس میں بھی ہاتھ سے شمار کرنے کی چنداں ضرورت نہیں بلکہ انگلیوں کے پوروں کو شمار کرے۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب جمیل احمد عفی عنہ
Counting verses and tasbihat in prayer is disliked. And it is disliked to count verses and tasbihat with the hand in prayer, and likewise counting surahs, because that is not from the actions of prayer. And from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) it is narrated that there is no harm in that in both fard and nafl prayers, out of observance of the sunnah of recitation and acting upon that which has come in the sunnah. We respond: It is possible for the one praying to count that before beginning, thus he becomes independent of counting afterwards. And Allah knows best. Explanation: The issue is that counting tasbihat and verses with the hand in prayer is makruh, whether the prayer is fard or nafl. Similarly, counting surahs is also makruh because counting verses, tasbihat, or surahs is not from the actions of prayer. This is the Zahir al-Riwayah. From the condition 'with the hand' it is understood that counting by pressing the finger joints or by the heart is not makruh. From the condition 'with the hand' it is also understood that one should not count with the tongue, because counting with the tongue invalidates the prayer. The author mentioned the condition 'in prayer' to indicate that outside prayer, counting is not makruh. But Allamah Fakhr al-Islam stated that outside prayer, counting tasbih is a bid'ah, and said that the Salaf used to say: 'We commit sins without counting, and we recite tasbih with counting.' This is a non-Zahir al-Riwayah narration from the Sahibayn that there is no harm in counting verses or tasbihat in both fard and nafl prayers. The proof of the Sahibayn is that sometimes a person needs to count verses, e.g., he wants to recite in fard prayer according to the sunnah method, i.e., recite forty or sixty verses as established from the Sunnah of the Prophet, or for example in Salat al-Tasbih, which is established by the Sunnah, he wants to act upon it. It is evident that in these two cases there is no alternative without counting. Therefore, counting at that time is not harmful. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa (referred to as 'Imam Abu Hanifa'? Actually 'Imam Abu Khalifa' is likely a corruption of 'Abu Hanifa'? But the text says 'Imam Abu Khalifa' but it seems to be 'Abu Hanifa' from context. Actually in the original, it says 'Imam Abu Hanifa' but OCR may have corrupted to 'خلیفہ'. We'll follow the text.) He said that acting on the sunnah recitation can also be achieved by counting before starting the prayer and specifying that in the first rak'ah I will recite from here to here, and in the second from here to here. Thus, there is no need to count during prayer. As for Salat al-Tasbih, in that too there is little need for counting with the hand; rather, one should count with the finger joints. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage contains a ruling and intra-Hanafi dispute regarding counting verses, tasbihat, and surahs with the hand during prayer. The author first states the Zahir al-Riwayah position: it is makruh to count with the hand in both fard and nafl prayers because such counting is not among the actions of prayer. However, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) report a contrary view that there is no harm in counting to follow the Sunnah of recitation (e.g., reciting a specific number of verses). The Hanafi position (Imam Abu Hanifa) responds that one can count before starting the prayer, so counting during prayer is unnecessary. The commentary adds details: counting with finger joints or in the heart is not makruh; counting with the tongue invalidates prayer. Outside prayer, counting is generally not makruh, but Fakhr al-Islam considers it bid'ah. The preferred view (mufta bihi) is the Zahir al-Riwayah: makruh, but the Sahibayn's view is also transmitted as a non-Zahir al-Riwayah opinion. The author (probably the Urdu commentator) supports the view that counting with finger joints is sufficient.

Key Terms
بالید (bil-yad): Literally 'with the hand'; specifies the means of counting that is makruh.
مفسد نماز (mufsid as-salah): That which invalidates prayer; here, speaking (counting with tongue) invalidates.
ظاہر الروایۃ (zahir al-riwayah): The established and relied-upon transmissions from the early Hanafi imams, specifically the six books of Imam Muhammad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is permissible (mubah).
B) It is disliked (makruh).
C) It invalidates the prayer.
D) It is recommended (sunnah).

Key Takeaway
Counting with the hand in prayer is makruh; the mufta bihi is the Zahir al-Riwayah position; use finger joints or count before prayer to avoid karahah.

Counting Ayat and Tasbih in Prayer: Ruling and Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on counting verses during prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on counting verses by hand during prayer and explain the dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Counting by hand in prayer is makruh in Zahir al-Riwayah, but necessity allows it per the Sahibayn.

This passage addresses a common question: can one count verses or tasbih on one's fingers during prayer? The Hanafi school has a nuanced answer. While the well-known transmitted position (Zahir al-Riwayah) holds it is disliked, the two principal disciples (Sahibayn) permitted it when necessary. Understanding this dispute helps you apply the correct ruling in daily worship.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position from Zahir al-Riwayah
Identify the ruling given in the text for counting by hand during prayer. Note that it is makruh because it is not from the acts of prayer.
The text explicitly says 'counting is also disliked because... this is the Zahir al-Riwayah.'
2
Identify the Sahibayn's view
Recognize that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that there is no harm in counting during prayer when necessary. Their view is recorded in non-Zahir al-Riwayah.
The Sahibayn allow counting in both fard and nafl prayers when needed.
3
Examine the Sahibayn's proof
Understand their reasoning: necessity arises when one must recite a specific number of verses (e.g., sunnah recitation in fard or Salat al-Tasbih), and counting is the only practical way to fulfill that.
They argue that without counting, one cannot properly observe the sunnah in those cases.
4
Analyze Imam Abu Hanifa's response
Imam Abu Hanifa counters that one can pre-count before prayer, rendering counting during prayer unnecessary. For Salat al-Tasbih, he suggests counting with finger joints, which is not disliked.
This is a rational proof (dalil aqli) showing an alternative method.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
The practical difference: the mufta bihi (operative ruling) is the Zahir al-Riwayah position of makruh. However, when necessity arises, a mufti may consider the Sahibayn's view. The qualification 'by hand' excludes counting mentally or by finger joints.
The text does not explicitly state mufta bihi, but the Zahir al-Riwayah carries greater authority.

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد دوم باب ما يفسد الصلوة وما يكره فيها شمار کرنا بھی مکروہ ہے کیونکہ آیات یا تسبیحات یا سورتوں کا شمار کرنا نماز کے اعمال سے نہیں ہے یہی ظاہر الروایۃ ہے بالید کی قید سے معلوم ہوا کہ انگلیوں کے پوروں سے دبا کر یا دل سے یاد کرنا مکروہ نہیں ہے۔ بالید کی قید سے یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ زبان سے شمار نہ کرے کیونکہ زبان سے شمار کرنا مفسد نماز ہے۔ مصنف نے فی الصلواۃ کی قید ذکر کر کے اس طرف اشارہ کر دیا کہ غیر نماز کی صورت میں شمار کرنا مکروہ نہیں ہے لیکن علامہ فخر الاسلام نے ذکر کیا کہ خارج صلوۃ بھی تسبیح کا شمار کرنا بدعت ہے اور فرمایا و كان السلف يقولون نذنب[؟] ولاتخصى و نسبح و لحضی[؟] یعنی اسلاف کہتے تھے کہ ہم گناہ تو بے شمار کرتے ہیں اور اس کو شمار نہیں کرتے، اور تسبیح پڑھتے ہیں تو شمار کرتے ہیں یہ غیر ظاہر الروایۃ میں صاحبین سے مروی ہے آیات یا تسبیحات کو فرائض اور نوافل دونوں میں شمار کرنے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ بسا اوقات انسان کو آیات شمار کرنے کی ضرورت پڑتی ہے مثلاً وہ چاہتا ہے کہ فرائض میں مسنون طریقہ پر قراءت کرے یعنی چالیس یا ساتھ آیات پڑھے جیسا کہ سنت رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم سے ثابت ہے یا مثلا صلوۃ التسبیح میں جس پر سنت وارد ہوئی ہے اس پر عمل کرنا چاہتا ہے۔ اب ظاہر ہے کہ ان دونوں صورتوں میں بغیر شمار کے کوئی چارہ کار نہیں ہے لہذا اس وقت شمار کرنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہوگا۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قراءت مسنونہ پر عمل اس طور پر بھی ہو سکتا ہے کہ نماز شروع کرنے سے پہلے شمار کر کے متعین کرلے کہ پہلی رکعت میں یہاں سے یہاں تک پڑھوں گا اور دوسری میں یہاں سے یہاں تک پڑھوں گا پس اس صورت میں نماز میں شمار کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں رہے گی۔ رہا صلوۃ التسبیح کا معاملہ تو اس میں بھی ہاتھ سے شمار کرنے کی چنداں ضرورت نہیں بلکہ انگلیوں کے پوروں کو شمار کرے۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب جمیل احمد عفی عنہ
Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary of Hidayah, Volume 2, Chapter: What invalidates prayer and what is disliked in it. Counting (verses) is also disliked because counting verses, tasbih, or surahs is not from the acts of prayer. This is the Zahir al-Riwayah. From the qualification 'with the hand' it is understood that counting by pressing the finger joints or by heart (mentally) is not disliked. From the qualification 'with the hand' it is also understood that one should not count with the tongue, because counting with the tongue invalidates the prayer. The author, by mentioning the qualification 'in prayer', indicated that counting outside of prayer is not disliked. But Allamah Fakhr al-Islam mentioned that counting tasbih even outside prayer is a bid'ah, and he said: 'The Salaf used to say: We commit sins without counting, and we recite tasbih and count it.' This is narrated from the Sahibayn in non-Zahir al-Riwayah. There is no harm in counting verses or tasbih in both fard and nafl prayers. The proof of the Sahibayn is that sometimes a person needs to count verses, for example, he wants to recite in fard prayer in the Sunnah manner, i.e., recite forty or more verses as established from the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), or for example, in Salat al-Tasbih, which is established in Sunnah, he wants to act upon it. It is obvious that in both cases there is no alternative without counting, so at that time there is no harm in counting. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is that one can act upon the Sunnah recitation by counting before starting the prayer and determining that in the first rak'ah I will recite from here to here, and in the second from here to here. Thus, in this case, there will be no need to count during the prayer. As for the matter of Salat al-Tasbih, even in that, there is no great need to count with the hand; rather, count with the finger joints. And Allah knows best what is correct. Jamil Ahmad, may he be forgiven.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding counting verses or tasbih during prayer. The text begins by stating the ruling from Zahir al-Riwayah: counting by hand is makruh because it is not from the acts of prayer. It then clarifies that counting by pressing finger joints or mentally is not disliked, but counting with the tongue invalidates prayer. The author notes that outside prayer, counting is not disliked, though a later authority, Fakhr al-Islam, says it is bid'ah even outside. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) narrate that there is no harm in counting in both fard and nafl, as necessity (e.g., reciting a specific number of verses in fard or performing Salat al-Tasbih) sometimes requires it. Imam Abu Hanifa counters that one can pre-count before prayer to determine the verses, thus eliminating the need to count during. He also suggests that for Salat al-Tasbih, one can count using finger joints, which is not disliked. The text does not explicitly rule on the mufta bihi, but it identifies the Zahir al-Riwayah as the position of makruh.

Key Terms
ظاہر الروایۃ (Zahir al-Riwayah): The well-known transmitted position from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani in his six core books.
صاحبین (Sahibayn): Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two principal disciples of Imam Abu Hanifa.
تسبیح (tasbih): Recitation of 'Subhanallah' or similar phrases of glorification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, counting by hand during prayer is makruh in the transmitted position, but the Sahibayn allow it when necessary, and the mufta bihi follows the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Ruling on the Mosque Rooftop: Prohibited Acts
Explains that the mosque rooftop shares the same ruling as the mosque interior.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for acts on the mosque rooftop and explain why it shares the ruling of the mosque, using the principle of qiyas.

Core Idea
The mosque rooftop shares the same legal rulings as the interior, so prohibited acts inside are also prohibited on the roof.

This passage addresses a common question: What is the legal status of the mosque rooftop? The Hanafi school clarifies that the rooftop is an integral part of the mosque. Therefore, acts that are forbidden inside the mosque due to its sanctity are also strongly disliked (makruh tahrimi) on the roof. The proof is based on analogy (qiyas) with the interior, supported by practical implications such as the validity of prayer while following an imam below, the non-invalidation of i'tikaf by ascending, and the prohibition for a junub to stand there.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Target Acts
Determine which specific acts are being ruled upon in the passage: sexual intercourse, urination, and defecation.
These acts are mentioned explicitly in the text.
2
Identify the Ruling for Each Act
State the hukm level for these acts on the mosque rooftop. The passage declares them makruh tahrimi.
Makruh tahrimi is close to haram and requires avoidance.
3
Understand the Legal Basis
The passage states the principle: because the rooftop has the ruling of the mosque (لان سطح المسجد له حكم المسجد). This is the illa for the analogy.
This principle is established through qiyas jaliy.
4
Examine the Supporting Proofs
The passage provides three practical consequences that confirm the rooftop's equivalence to the mosque: validity of following the imam below, non-invalidation of i'tikaf, and prohibition for a junub to stand.
These are not independent proofs but corroborating evidence.
5
Apply the Ruling to New Cases
Consider other acts prohibited inside the mosque, such as eating, sleeping, or trading; the same ruling applies on the rooftop unless there is a specific exception.
Use the principle of qiyas to extend the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسجد کی چھت پر ولی، پیشاب پاخانہ مکروہ تحریمی ہے یکره المجامعة فوق المسجد والبول والتخلى لان سطح المسجد له حكم المسجد حتى يصح الاقتداء بمن تحته ولا يبطل الاعتكاف بالصعود اليه ولا يحل للجنب الوقوف عليه ويكره المجامعة فوق المسجد والبول والتخلى لان سطح المسجد له حكم المسجد تشریح مسئلہ مسجد کی چھت پر جماع کرنا پیشاب پاخانہ کرنا کرہ تحریمی ہے کیونکہ مسجد کی چھت کا وہی حکم ہے جو مسجد کا ہے۔ کیونکہ چھت پر کھڑے ہو کر کوئی شخص اس امام کی اقتداء کرے جو نیچے ہے تو شرعاً درست ہے۔ اور مسجد کی چھت پر چڑھنے کی وجہ سے اعتکاف باطل نہیں ہوتا۔ اور جنبی کے لئے مسجد کی چھت پر کھڑا ہونا جائز نہیں ہے۔ جس طرح کہ مسجد کے اندر کھڑا ہونا جائز نہیں۔
On the rooftop of the mosque, sexual intercourse and urination/defecation are makruh tahrimi. It is disliked to have intercourse on the mosque rooftop, and to urinate and defecate, because the rooftop of the mosque has the ruling of the mosque, even to the point that following (in prayer) the one below is valid, and i'tikaf is not invalidated by ascending to it, and it is not permissible for a junub to stand on it. And it is disliked to have intercourse on the mosque rooftop, and to urinate and defecate, because the rooftop of the mosque has the ruling of the mosque. Commentary: The issue is that having intercourse on the mosque rooftop, and urinating and defecating, are makruh tahrimi because the rooftop of the mosque has the same ruling as the mosque. Because if a person stands on the rooftop and follows the imam who is below, it is valid. And i'tikaf is not invalidated by ascending to the rooftop. And it is not permissible for a junub to stand on the rooftop, just as it is not permissible to stand inside the mosque.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the mosque rooftop. It first states that sexual intercourse, urination, and defecation on the rooftop are makruh tahrimi due to the legal principle that the rooftop shares the same ruling as the mosque. The proof is shown through consequences: prayer following the imam below is valid, i'tikaf is not broken by ascending, and a junub is not allowed to stand there. The analogy (qiyas) is clear: the rooftop is part of the mosque's structure, so it retains the mosque's sacred status. The commentary emphasizes that just as these acts are forbidden inside the mosque, they are also disliked on the roof.

Key Terms
سطح المسجد (sath al-masjid): The roof of the mosque, considered legally part of the mosque.
حكم المسجد (hukm al-masjid): The legal ruling that applies to a mosque, including sanctity and restrictions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The rooftop of a mosque is legally equivalent to the interior, so all prohibitions apply equally.

Ruling on Locking the Mosque Door
Default ruling with a conditional exception based on necessity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default ruling on locking the mosque door, identify the Quranic proof, and apply the exception when property is at risk.

Core Idea
Locking the mosque door is disliked but allowed when fear for property necessitates it.

The matn from al-Hidayah begins with a clear default: locking the mosque door is makruh (disliked) because it resembles preventing prayer, which is haram. However, the text immediately introduces a concession: if there is genuine fear for the mosque's property (such as theft), particularly outside prayer times, then there is no harm in locking. This lesson explores the legal reasoning behind the dislike and the scope of the exception, showing how Hanafi fiqh balances principle with practical necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Default Ruling
Read the first sentence of the matn: 'يكره ان يغلق باب المسجد'. Recognize that the default hukm is makruh (specifically makruh tahrimi in Hanafi terminology).
The word 'يكره' indicates dislike, not outright prohibition.
2
Locate the Dalil
The passage cites Quran 2:114 as evidence: 'وَمَنْ أَظْلَمُ مِمَّنْ مَّنَعَ مَسَاجِدَ اللهِ أَنْ يُذْكَرَ فِيهَا اسْمُه'. Understand that locking resembles prevention, hence the dislike.
The dalil is qati' al-thubut (Quran) but zanni al-dalalah (it implies prevention, not explicitly locking).
3
Identify the Exception and Its Conditions
The phrase 'وقيل لاباس به اذا خيف على متاع المسجد' introduces a concession. Extract the conditions: fear for property (الخوف على متاع المسجد) and time (outside prayer times, implied by 'في غير أوقات الصلوة').
The exception changes the ruling from makruh to mubah (permissible).
4
Understand the Thamarah al-Khilaf
Note that there is a difference of opinion: some scholars allow locking even without fear (mubah), while the Hanafi default is makruh. The practical difference lies in the default attitude toward locking when no necessity exists.
The Hanafi position is cautious to avoid resembling prevention of prayer.

اور مسجد کا دروازہ مقفل کرنا مکروہ ہے کیونکہ یہ نماز سے روکنے کے مشابہ ہے اور کہا گیا کہ کچھ مضائقہ نہیں جب کہ مسجد کے ان پر خوف ہو سوائے اوقات نماز کے۔
انا مسئلہ مسجد کا دروازہ بند رکھنا مکروہ ہے کیونکہ یہ نماز سے روکنے کے مشابہ ہے اور نماز سے روکنا حرام ہے۔ خداوند قدوس کا ارشاد وَمَنْ أَظْلَمُ مِمَّنْ مَّنَعَ مَسَاجِدَ اللهِ أَنْ يُذْكَرَ فِيهَا اسْمُه یعنی اس سے بڑا ظالم کون ہوگا جو مساجد میں اللہ کا ذکر کرنے سے منع

ر ان کے دور میں مساجد کے دروازوں کو بند رکھنے میں کوئی قباحت نہیں ہوگی بلکہ ٹھیک ہوگا۔
It is disliked to lock the door of the mosque because it resembles preventing prayer. It has been said there is no harm if one fears for the goods of the mosque outside of prayer times. And the issue is that locking the mosque door is disliked because it resembles preventing prayer, and preventing prayer is haram. Allah Almighty said: 'And who is more unjust than one who prevents the mosques of Allah from His name being mentioned therein.' Some scholars said that if there is fear of loss or theft of mosque property, then there is no objection to locking the door, because people's conditions vary due to the change of times. Similarly, women were once allowed in mosques, but when fear of fitna arose, they were prevented; thus in such times, locking mosque doors is proper.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the dislike of locking the mosque door. The matn states it is makruh, with the proof being its resemblance to preventing prayer, which is haram (supported by Quran 2:114). However, there is a concession: if there is fear for the mosque's property (like theft), it becomes permissible, especially outside prayer times. The sharh extends this by citing the analogy of women's attendance changing with times, indicating that rulings can adapt based on circumstances. The default position is that locking is makruh tahrimi, but necessity permits it.

Key Terms
يكره (yukrah): It is disliked; in Hanafi terms, makruh tahrimi for locking the mosque door.
المنع من الصلوة (al-man' min al-salah): Preventing prayer; the text uses this as the illa (reason) for the dislike of locking.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Permissible (mubah).
B) Disliked (makruh).
C) Forbidden (haram).
D) Recommended (mustahabb).

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi default is that locking the mosque door is makruh tahrimi, but necessity (fear for property, outside prayer times) makes it permissible.

Ruling on Decorating Mosques with Plaster, Wood, and Gold Water
Ruling with proof on mosque decoration from Hidayah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mosque decoration, identify the source of funds that changes the ruling, and explain the evidence from Umar's practice.

Core Idea
Decorating mosques is permissible from personal wealth but forbidden for a waqf trustee using endowment funds.

The decoration of mosques is a topic that touches on both the aesthetic dimension of worship and the strict rules of waqf management. The Hanafi school, drawing on the practice of Umar al-Faruq, permits the adornment of mosques from one's own wealth, but strictly curtails the use of endowment funds for non-structural purposes. This lesson will walk you through the ruling, the evidence, and the scholarly dispute that surrounds this issue.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act is decorating the mosque with materials like plaster, wood, and gold water. The matn states 'la ba's' (no harm), which in Hanafi usul indicates permissibility (mubah) without reward or sin.
2
Distinguish the source of funds
The ruling changes based on who pays. If done from personal wealth, it is mubah. If the mutawalli (trustee) uses waqf funds, he may only spend on structural integrity; decoration is forbidden and he is personally liable.
3
Examine the Hanafi evidence
The primary evidence is the action of Umar ibn al-Khattab, who expanded and adorned the mosque during his caliphate. This practice by a major Companion is a proof of permissibility.
4
Understand the opposing view
Some scholars, including Ali ibn Abi Talib, considered mosque decoration makruh, citing the hadith about the signs of the Day of Judgment and the idea that simplicity is better.
5
Identify the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon Hanafi position, as given in the Hidayah, is that mosque decoration is mubah from personal wealth, and the mutawalli is restricted and liable if he acts otherwise.

There is no harm in adorning the mosque with plaster, teak wood, and gold water. The author's statement 'la ba's' indicates that the one who does so will neither be rewarded nor sin; it is said it is a good deed. This applies when done from one's own wealth. As for the mutawalli, he should only do from waqf property that which relates to the strength of the building, not that which relates to decoration. If he does so, he is liable. Allah knows best. (Translation of Urdu commentary): There is no harm in adorning mosques with plaster, wood, and gold water. The author's statement 'la ba's' indicates that the one who does so will not be rewarded nor sin. Some said it is worship. This is when done from personal wealth. As for the mutawalli, he should only do from waqf funds that which strengthens the building, not decoration; if he does, he is liable. People differ on this: some considered it makruh, citing Ali's statement upon seeing a decorated mosque, and the hadith counting mosques among the signs of the Day of Judgment. Walid ibn Abd al-Malik spent much on adorning the Prophet's mosque, and Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz gave it to the needy. Hanafi jurists say there is no harm, with evidence that Umar al-Faruq expanded and adorned the mosque. Also, adornment attracts people to i'tikaf, which is good. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi said the matn's 'la ba's' indicates no reward or sin. Some said it is worship, with evidence from the verse 'The mosques of Allah are only to be maintained by those who believe in Allah and the Last Day' and the Kaaba being adorned with gold, silver, and silk. Ibn al-Humam said adornment of mosques is worship because it honors them. The author of Hidayah said that adornment being worship or permissible is when the mutawalli spends his own lawful wealth, not the waqf funds. The mutawalli is liable if he uses waqf funds for decoration. Abu Bakr al-Razi reported that in our time, due to fear of oppressors, leftover funds may be used for strengthening.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the permissibility of decorating mosques. The matn states 'la ba's' (no harm), which the sharh interprets as neither reward nor sin when done from personal wealth. The commentary then presents a dispute: some scholars (including Ali and others) deem it makruh, citing simplicity of mosques and avoiding extravagance. However, Hanafis argue it is permissible, citing Umar's expansion and the benefit of attracting people to worship (e.g., i'tikaf). The decisive point is the source of funds: if from personal lawful wealth, it is permissible; if from waqf, the mutawalli must only use funds for structural integrity, not decoration, and is personally liable if he does otherwise. The Hanafi position is that it is not makruh but also not necessarily a reward (some say it is rewardable).

Key Terms
لا بأس (la ba's): No harm; indicates permissibility, but with no reward and no sin in this context.
متولی (mutawalli): The administrator or trustee of a waqf; he is restricted in using waqf funds only for essential purposes.
وقف (waqf): Endowment; property dedicated for charitable purposes; its funds must be used as specified by the donor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a mutawalli using waqf funds to decorate a mosque with gold water?
A) Permissible, as it beautifies the house of Allah.
B) Permissible, but the mutawalli is rewarded.
C) Not permissible; the mutawalli is liable to compensate.
D) Makruh but valid.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of mosque decoration hinges on the source of funds: personal wealth permits it (mubah), while waqf funds restrict it to structural maintenance; the trustee is liable for any misuse.

The Legal Status of Witr: Wajib or Sunnah?
Intra-Hanafi dispute with dalil naqli and usul analysis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifa considers Witr wajib, state the Sahibayn's counter-argument, and identify the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Witr is wajib by the Prophet's command; the Sahibayn's signs of sunnah do not override the imperative.

This lesson explores one of the most significant intra-Hanafi ikhtilafat: is Witr prayer wajib or sunnah? Abu Hanifa holds it is wajib, while his two main students consider it sunnah. We will examine both proofs, understand the usul principles at play, and see why the school ultimately adopts Abu Hanifa's view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
State the precise legal question: Is Witr prayer wajib or sunnah? Note that it is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad).
There is also an outlier view that it is fard (Imam Zufar and Malikis).
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof
Examine the hadith cited: 'Allah has added a prayer for you, indeed it is Witr, so pray it between Isha and dawn.' Identify the imperative 'pray it' (فصلوها). Apply Hanafi usul: a command (amr) indicates obligation (wujub). Note the consensus on making up missed Witr as supporting evidence.
The hadith is ahad, so thubut is zanni, but the command still establishes wujub, not fard.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn argue that Witr shows 'signs of sunnah': its denier is not declared an unbeliever, and no specific adhan is called. They also cite a hadith where the Prophet limited obligatory prayers to five, implying that all beyond that are voluntary.
They use a general principle: absence of takfir indicates non-obligation.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa responds that the specific command for Witr overrides the general five-prayer hadith. The absence of takfir does not negate wujub, as wujub can be established through ahad hadith. The consensus on qada confirms wajib status.
This shows the Hanafi methodology of preferring specific (khass) over general (amm).
5
Determine the thamarah and tarjih
The practical difference: if Witr is wajib, missing it is sinful and requires qada; if sunnah, omission is not sinful. The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is that Witr is wajib, following Abu Hanifa.
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah presents Abu Hanifa's view as the primary position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلوة الـــوتــــر
ترجمہ (یہ) باب نماز وتر کے بیان میں) ہے۔
باب صلوة الوتر
تری جب مصنف علیہ الرحمہ مفروضات اور ان کے متعلقات یعنی اوقات ، کیفیت ادا اور ادا کامل اور قاصر کے بیان سے فارغ ہو کے نواب اس باب کے تحت اس نماز کا بیان ہے جو فرض سے کمتر اور نقل سے برتر ہے یعنی صلوٰۃ وتر۔ اس مناسبت کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ آگے وافل کا بیان ہے۔ پس واجب یعنی وتر کو فرض اور نفل کے درمیان میں ذکر کیا گیا ہے جیسا کہ اس کا حق ہے۔
وتر کی شرعی حیثیت... اقوال فقہاء و دلائل
الموتر واجب عند أبي حنيفة وقالا سنة لظهور آثار السنن فيه حيث لا يكفر جاحده ولا يؤذن له ولابي حنيفة قوله عليه السلام أن الله تعالى زادكم صلاة ألا وهى الوتر فصلوها ما بين العشاء الى طلوع الفجر امر وهو الوجوب ولهذا وجب القضاء بالإجماع وإنما لا يكفر جاحده لان وجوبه ثبت بالسنة وهو المعنى بما روى نه انه سنة وهو يؤدى فى وقت العشاء فاكتفى بأذانه وإقامته رجمہ وتر امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک واجب ہے۔ اور صاحبین نے کہا کہ وتر سنت ہے۔ کیونکہ وتر میں سنتوں کے آثار ظاہر ہیں۔ چنانچہ منکر کا فرنہیں ہوتا۔ اور وتر کے لئے اذان نہیں ہے۔ اور ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے تمہارے واسطے کی نماز زائد فرمائی ہے۔ آگاہ رہو کہ وہ وتر ہے۔ پس اس کو عشاء اور طلوع فجر کے درمیان پڑھو۔ حدیث میں امر ہے اور امر وجوب کے کے آتا ہے اسی وجہ سے وتر کی قضاء بالا جماع واجب ہے اور اس کے منکر کی تکفیر اس لئے نہیں ہوتی کہ اس کا وجوب سنت سے ثابت ہے۔ ری کا معنی ہیں اس قول کے جو ابو حنیفہ سے مروی ہے کہ وتر سنت ہے اور وتر چونکہ عشاء کے وقت میں ادا کیا جاتا ہے۔ تو عشاء کی اذان را قامت پر اکتفاء کیا گیا۔
ایا وتر کے مسئلہ میں امام ابوحنیفہ سے تین روایات ہیں اول یہ کہ وتر واجب ہے۔ دوم یہ کہ وتر سنت مؤکدہ ہے اس کو صاحبین اور رانی نے اختیار کیا ہے۔ سوم یہ کہ وتر فرض ہے یہ قول امام زفر اور مالکیہ کا ہے۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وتر میں سنتوں کے آثار ظاہر بیٹا سنتوں کی طرح وتر کا منکر کا فرنہیں ہے۔ اور نہ ہی وتر کے لئے اذان دی جاتی جیسا کہ سنتوں کے لئے اذان نہیں ہوتی ۔ پس
وم ہوا کہ وتر سنت ہے۔
صاحب شرح نقایہ نے صاحبین کی طرف سے نقلی دلیل بھی بیان فرمائی ہے دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ایک اعرابی سے فرمایا تھا حمس صلوة كتبهن الله عليك قال هل على غيرها قل لا الا ان تطوع يعنی اللہ جل شانہ نے تجھ پر پانچ نمازیں فرض کی زیر اعرابی نے کہا کہ اس کے علاوہ بھی مجھ پر فرض ہے۔ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ نہیں مگر یہ کہ نفل پڑھے۔ اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ پانچ ان کی نمازوں کے علاوہ سب نقل ہیں لہذا وتر کا واجب ہونا ثابت نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ وتر بھی پانچ نمازوں کے علاوہ ہے۔
Chapter of Witr Prayer. When the author completed the obligations and their pertaining matters (times, performance, complete and deficient), he mentions in this chapter the prayer that is below fard and above nafl, i.e., Witr. The appropriateness is that after this comes nawafil. So the wajib (Witr) is placed between fard and nafl, as is its right.
The legal status of Witr: Witr is wajib according to Abu Hanifa. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said it is sunnah, because the signs of sunnah are apparent in it: its denier is not declared an unbeliever, and no adhan is called for it. Abu Hanifa's proof is the hadith: 'Allah has added a prayer for you, indeed it is Witr, so pray it between Isha and dawn.' This is a command, and a command indicates obligation. Therefore, making it up is obligatory by consensus. Its denier is not declared an unbeliever because its obligation is established by sunnah (not Quran). The meaning is what is narrated: that it is sunnah and it is performed during Isha's time, so its adhan and iqamah suffice.
There are three narrations from Abu Hanifa: (1) Witr is wajib; (2) Witr is sunnah mu'akkadah, adopted by the two and [another narrator]; (3) Witr is fard, a view of Imam Zufar and Malikiyyah. The two's proof is that signs of sunnah are apparent in Witr: its denier is not declared an unbeliever, and no adhan is called for it, like sunnah prayers. So Witr is sunnah. The author of Sharh al-Niqayah also cited a transmitted proof: the Prophet told a Bedouin, 'Five prayers Allah has prescribed upon you.' He asked, 'Is there any other upon me?' He said, 'No, unless you pray voluntarily.' This shows that besides the five, all are nafl, so Witr cannot be wajib since it is outside the five.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on Witr prayer and immediately addresses the central intra-Hanafi dispute regarding its legal status. The author of Al-Hidayah states that Witr is wajib according to Abu Hanifa, while the two companions (Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold it to be sunnah. The reasoning of the Sahibayn is based on two 'signs of sunnah': (1) denying Witr does not lead to takfir (declaration of unbelief), whereas denying an obligatory act typically does; (2) no specific adhan is called for Witr, just as with sunnah prayers. These indicators suggest it is sunnah. Abu Hanifa's proof is the authentic hadith in which the Prophet directly commanded the performance of Witr—'So pray it' is an imperative (amr), and according to Hanafi usul, a command from the Prophet that is not qualified by a permissive context establishes obligation (wujub). Although the command is from the Prophet (not directly from the Quran), it is still a binding proof in Hanafi law. The fact that making up missed Witr is obligatory by consensus (ijma') further supports its wajib status. However, the denier is not declared an unbeliever because its obligation is established through a sunnah (hadith ahad), not through a Quranic text or mutawatir sunnah. The passage then notes three narrations from Abu Hanifa himself: (1) wajib (the strongest and adopted in the school), (2) sunnah mu'akkadah (preferred by Sahibayn and some other narrators), and (3) fard (held by Imam Zufar and the Malikis). The Sahibayn also cite a hadith where the Prophet told a Bedouin that only five prayers are obligatory, implying that any prayer beyond those five is voluntary, which would include Witr. However, Abu Hanifa responds that the command for Witr is specific and comes from a later hadith, so it is an exception to the general rule. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is that Witr is wajib, a distinct category between fard and sunnah. This lesson exemplifies how the Hanafi school uses usul al-fiqh principles—particularly the interpretation of commands (amr) and the significance of consensus (ijma') in weighing evidences—to derive rulings.

Key Terms
وتر (witr): The odd-numbered prayer performed after Isha, consisting of three rak'at, with a specific du'a (qunut). It is distinct from the five daily prayers.
صاحبین (al-Sahibayn): Refers to the two principal students of Abu Hanifa: Imam Abu Yusuf (d. 182 AH) and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (d. 189 AH). Their views often carry significant weight in the school.
امر (amr): A command; a linguistic form (usually imperative) that indicates a demand. In Hanafi usul, the default ruling from a command is obligation (wujub) unless a contrary indicator is present.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is Witr considered wajib rather than sunnah?
A) Because the Quran explicitly commands Witr in Surah al-Fatihah.
B) Because the Prophet's command 'pray Witr' is an imperative which indicates obligation in Hanafi usul.
C) Because missing Witr is punishable by death.
D) Because there is consensus that Witr is wajib.

Key Takeaway
Witr is wajib in the Hanafi school, established by the Prophet's command and consensus on qada, despite the Sahibayn's contrary view.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
The Legal Status of Witr Prayer: Wajib, Sunnah, or Fard?
Dispute over Witr's status with proofs and rebuttals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school classifies Witr as wajib and evaluate the proofs from the Sahibayn and other schools.

Core Idea
Witr is wajib in the Hanafi school because its proof is a command from a non-mutawatir hadith, establishing an obligation below fard.

The Witr prayer occupies a unique position in Hanafi fiqh: it is not a fard, nor a sunnah, but a wajib—a distinct category of obligation. This lesson examines the intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute over its legal status, focusing on the proofs and rebuttals presented by Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn. Understanding this dispute illuminates the Hanafi usul principle that the imperative form (amr) from a zanni source indicates wujub.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa (wajib) and the Sahibayn (sunnah). Note the third opinion of Imam Zufar (fard).
The Hanafi school's mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.
2
Identify the opposing proofs
List the Sahibayn's rational proof (sunnah characteristics like no kufr for denier, no adhan) and textual proofs (Bedouin hadith, Ibn Umar camel hadith).
The opposing school also includes Shafi'i and Maliki views.
3
Follow the Hanafi response
Examine the Hanafi rebuttals: denier not kafir due to zanni proof; Bedouin hadith abrogated; Ibn Umar hadith contradictory.
The response reinforces the strength of the imperative hadith.
4
Analyse the Hanafi dalil
Study the hadith 'إن الله تعالى زادكم صلاة ألا وهي الوتر فصلوها...' and the three arguments: attribution to Allah, addition implies limited (so fard-like), and imperative indicates wujub.
The zanni thubut prevents it from becoming fard, so it is wajib.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Contrast the practical consequences: if wajib, missing it requires qada and is sinful; if sunnah, no qada and no sin. This affects daily practice.
The Hanafi school follows the wajib ruling, so qada is obligatory.
