اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو بدایه اشرف البه
دوم یہ کہ حین میں ابن عمر سے مروی ہے ان النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم اوتر علی البعير یعنی نبی کریم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے وتر کی نماز سواری پر پڑ گیا بات ظاہر ہے کہ سواری پرنفل نماز ادا کی جاسکتی ہے نہ کہ فرض اور واجب پس اگر وتر کی نماز واجب ہوتی تو آنحضرت سواری قال السو نہ فرماتے۔
الحب
امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل حضور کا یہ قول ہے ان الله تعالی زادكم صلوة الا وهي الوتر فصلوهات مالك العشاء الى طلوع الفجر صاحب عنایہ نے لکھا ہے کہ اس حدیث سے چند طریقوں پر استدلال کیا گیا ہے۔ اول یہ کہ زبان ترجمہ نسبت اللہ کی طرف کی گئی ہے اور سنتوں کی نسبت رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کی طرف کی جاتی پس اگر وتر کی نماز سنت ہوتی تو حدیث میں بجا۔ طرف نسبت کرنے کے رسول کی طرف نسبت کی جاتی لیکن چونکہ رسول کی طرف نسبت نہیں کی گئی اس لئے وتر کی نماز سنت نہیں ہیں چاہتے ۔ ایک قول واجب ہوگی۔
کرچکے
تشریح
دوم یہ کہ کسی چیز پر زیادتی اسی وقت ہوتی ہے جبکہ شی مزید عليه (جس پر زیادتی کی گئی ہو محدود العد واد به مسلم ہے کہ نوافل غیر محدود ہیں ان کی کوئی انتہا نہیں پس زیادتی فرائض پر ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ محدود العدد ہیں اور چونکہ مزید (جس کی زیاد گئی ) کا مزید علیہا کے ہم جنس ہونا ضروی ہے اس لئے اس کی مقتضی یہ ہے کہ فرائض پر جس چیز کی زیادت کی گئی یعنی وتر کی بھی ، اسلاموں مگر چونکہ حدیث خبر واحد ہونے کی وجہ دلیل غیر قطعی ہے اور دلیل غیر قطعی سے واجب تو ثابت ہو سکتا ہے لیکن فرض ثابت نہیں ہو تار اور میان وتر واجب ہوگا۔
سلاموال
ليا
ایا سوم یہ کہ حدیث مذکور میں فصلوها امر کا صیغہ اور امر وجوب کے لئے آتا ہے لہذا اس سے بھی وتر کا وجوب ثابت ہوگا۔ صاحب ھدایہ نے کہا کہ وتر چونکہ واجب ہے اس لئے اس کی قضاء واجب ہوتی ہے ورنہ سنتوں کی قضاء واجب نہیں ہوا المقال صاحب کی تائید اس حدیث سے بھی ہوتی ہے کہ سردار دو جہاں صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ الوتر حق واجب فمن لم يوتر فليس دا است و تر حق واجب ہے جس نے وتر کی نماز نہیں پڑھی وہ ہم میں سے نہیں ہے (ابو داؤد) مسلم شریف میں ابوسعید خدری کی حدیث - لئے پر النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال او تــروا قبل ان تصبحوا یعنی حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ صبح ہونے سے پہلے پہلے وتر پڑھ لو۔ اس حدیث میں میں اتر امر کا صیغہ ہے جو وجوب پر دلالت کرتا ہے۔ صاحبین کی طرف سے پیش کردہ عقلی دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ وتر کا منکر کافر اس لئے نہیں ہوتا کہ وتر کا ثبوت سنت غیر متواتر ہے اور یہ جو امام ابو حنیفہ سے روایت ہے کہ وتر سنت ہے اس کے معنی بھی یہی ہیں کہ وتر کا ثبوتو سنت سے ہے اور چونکہ وتر کی نماز وقت میں ادا کی جاتی ہے اس لئے عشاء کی اذان اور اقامت پر اکتفاء کیا گیا۔ وتر کے لئے علیحدہ اذان واقامت کی ضرورت نہیں صاحبین کی طرف سے پیش کردہ حدیث اعرابی کا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہ حدیث وجوب و تر سے پہلے کی ہے۔ اور حدیث ابن عمر اونہ البعير کا جواب بقول طحاوی کے یہ ہے کہ حدیث ابن عمر ، حدیث حنظلہ بن ابی سفیان عن نافع عن ابن عمر کے معارض ہے۔ مدین کے الفاظ یہ ہیں انه كان يصلى على راحلته و يوتر بالارض و يزعم ان النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم فعل ذلک یعنی ابن عمرانی نماز پڑھتے تھے مگروتر زمین پر پڑھتے ۔ اور ابن عمر فرماتے تھے کہ نبی نے یہی کیا یعنی وتر کی نماز زمین پر ادا کی۔ پس جب ابن عمر روایتوں میں تعارض واقع ہو گیا تو دونوں ساقط ہو جائیں گی۔
Chapter of Witr Prayer. Translation: This chapter is about the Witr prayer. When the author (may Allah have mercy on him) finished discussing the obligatory prayers and their related matters (times, method of performance, complete and deficient performance), he now under this chapter discusses the prayer that is below obligatory and above voluntary, i.e., the Witr prayer. The reason for this arrangement is that voluntary prayers are discussed later. So the obligatory (wajib), i.e., Witr, is mentioned between obligatory (fard) and voluntary (nafl), as is its due. The legal status of Witr: Statements of jurists and proofs. Witr is wajib according to Abu Hanifa, and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said it is sunnah due to the appearance of sunnah characteristics in it, since its denier is not declared an unbeliever and no adhan is called for it. For Abu Hanifa is his statement (peace be upon him): 'Indeed Allah has added for you a prayer, and it is Witr, so pray it between Isha and the break of dawn.' The command indicates obligation, and therefore making it up (qada) is obligatory by consensus. Its denier is not declared an unbeliever only because its obligation is established by the Sunnah, and this is the meaning of what is reported from him that it is sunnah. And since it is performed in the time of Isha, its adhan and iqamah suffice. Summary: Witr is wajib according to Imam Abu Hanifa, and the Sahibayn said it is sunnah because the signs of sunnah are apparent in it: its denier is not declared an unbeliever, and no adhan is called for it. Abu Hanifa's proof is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Allah has added for you a prayer. Be aware that it is Witr. So pray it between Isha and the break of dawn.' The hadith contains a command, and a command indicates obligation. For this reason, making up Witr is obligatory by consensus. Its denier is not declared an unbeliever because its obligation is established by the Sunnah (non-mutawatir). The meaning of what is reported from Abu Hanifa that Witr is sunnah is that its proof is from the Sunnah, and because Witr is performed in the time of Isha, the adhan and iqamah of Isha suffice. Know that regarding the issue of Witr, three narrations are attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa: first that Witr is wajib, second that it is sunnah mu'akkadah (which the Sahibayn and [Rani?] adopted), third that it is fard, which is the saying of Imam Zufar and the Malikis. The Sahibayn's proof is that the signs of sunnah are apparent in Witr, just like the sunnah prayers; its denier is not declared an unbeliever, and no adhan is called for it, as for sunnah prayers. So they concluded that it is sunnah. The author of Sharh al-Niqayah has also transmitted a textual proof from the Sahibayn: the Prophet (peace be upon him) said to a Bedouin: 'Five prayers which Allah has prescribed for you.' He said: 'Is there any other (obligatory) upon me?' He said: 'No, unless you perform voluntary prayers.' This hadith shows that besides these five, all are voluntary, so Witr cannot be wajib because it is also among those outside the five. Second, Ibn Umar reported that the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed Witr on his camel. It is evident that only voluntary prayer can be performed on a mount, not obligatory or wajib. So if Witr were wajib, the Prophet would not have performed it on a mount. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is the Prophet's saying: 'Indeed Allah has added for you a prayer, and it is Witr, so pray it between Isha and the break of dawn.' The author of al-Inayah wrote that several arguments are derived from this hadith. First: The prayer is attributed to Allah, whereas sunan are attributed to the Prophet. So if Witr were sunnah, it would be attributed to the Prophet. Since it is not, Witr is not sunnah but wajib. Second: An addition (ziyadah) is only made to something that is limited in number. Voluntary prayers are unlimited, so the addition must be to the obligatory prayers, which are limited. And since the added thing must be of the same type as that to which it is added, Witr must be like the obligatory prayers. However, because the hadith is a khabar wahid (non-mutawatir), which is a non-definitive proof, obligation (wajib) can be established from it, but not fard. Therefore, Witr is wajib. Third: The hadith contains the imperative 'fassalluha', and a command indicates obligation. Therefore, obligation is established from it. The author of al-Hidayah said that since Witr is wajib, its makeup (qada) is obligatory; otherwise, makeup of sunnah prayers is not obligatory. This is supported by the hadith: 'Witr is a binding duty (haqq wajib). Whoever does not perform Witr is not from us.' And in Sahih Muslim, Abu Sa'id al-Khudri reported that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Perform Witr before dawn.' This hadith contains a command, which indicates obligation. The response to the Sahibayn's rational proof (about not declaring the denier an unbeliever) is that Witr's proof is from non-mutawatir Sunnah, which is why the denier is not declared an unbeliever. And what is reported from Abu Hanifa that Witr is sunnah means that its proof is from the Sunnah, and since Witr is performed in the time of Isha, the adhan and iqamah of Isha suffice; no separate adhan and iqamah are needed. The response to the Bedouin hadith is that it was before the obligation of Witr. The response to Ibn Umar's hadith about the camel, according to al-Tahawi, is that it is contradicted by the hadith of Hanzalah ibn Abi Sufyan from Nafi' from Ibn Umar, with the wording: 'He (Ibn Umar) used to pray on his mount but would perform Witr on the ground, claiming that the Prophet did that.' So when Ibn Umar's narrations contradict each other, both fall.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the legal status of the Witr prayer. The passage opens with the chapter heading 'Bab Salat al-Witr' and explains that the author places the discussion of Witr between the obligatory (fard) and voluntary (nafl) prayers because Witr holds an intermediate status: it is wajib, which in Hanafi terminology is a distinct category between fard and sunnah. The core dispute is between Imam Abu Hanifa, who holds Witr to be wajib, and the Sahibayn (Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani), who consider it sunnah. A third opinion from Imam Zufar and the Malikis holds that it is fard. The passage then presents the proofs. Imam Abu Hanifa's primary evidence is the hadith: 'Indeed Allah has added for you a prayer, and it is Witr, so pray it between Isha and the break of dawn.' The Hanafi argument is that the imperative 'fassalluha' indicates obligation (wujub) according to Hanafi usul al-fiqh, where a command from a non-mutawatir source establishes wujub, not fard. Additionally, the attribution of the prayer to Allah (rather than the Prophet) indicates it is not sunnah, as sunnah prayers are typically attributed to the Prophet. The passage also notes that making up Witr (qada) is obligatory by consensus, which further supports its wajib status. The Sahibayn's arguments include that Witr shares characteristics of sunnah prayers: its denier is not declared an unbeliever, and no separate adhan is called for it. They also cite the hadith of the Bedouin, where the Prophet said that only five prayers are obligatory, and the hadith of Ibn Umar that the Prophet performed Witr on his camel (indicating it is voluntary, as obligatory prayers cannot be performed on a mount). The passage then provides Hanafi responses to each objection. The Bedouin hadith is abrogated or predates the obligation of Witr. The camel hadith of Ibn Umar is contradicted by another narration from Ibn Umar himself, where he performed Witr on the ground, so both fall. The passage concludes by affirming the Hanafi position that Witr is wajib, with its makeup being obligatory, and emphasizes that Witr is not fard because its proof is from a non-mutawatir source, which establishes wujub but not fard. This is a classic example of intra-Hanafi ijtihad and the use of usul principles to derive rulings.

Key Terms
وتر (witr): The Witr prayer, a prayer performed after Isha and before dawn, consisting of an odd number of rak'ahs (typically three in the Hanafi school).
واجب (wajib): An obligation established by a non-certain (zanni) proof, such as a khabar wahid. Its omission is sinful, but its denier is not declared an unbeliever.
سنة (sunnah): A recommended act that the Prophet regularly performed. Its omission is not sinful, though the one who abandons it may be blameworthy.
أمر (amr): A command form in Arabic; according to Hanafi usul, it indicates obligation (wujub) unless there is a contextual indication (qarinah) to the contrary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Imam Abu Hanifa consider Witr prayer wajib rather than sunnah?
A) Because the hadith about Witr is mutawatir, making it fard.
B) Because the hadith contains an imperative command, and according to Hanafi usul, a command from a non-mutawatir source indicates wujub.
C) Because Witr is performed in congregation.
D) Because the Prophet always performed it and said it is sunnah.

Key Takeaway
Witr is wajib in the Hanafi school; its omission requires qada, and its status is established by a command from a non-mutawatir hadith.
